Over the years, millions of students at all different levels have consumed our learning content and worked through courses and codelabs to advance their skills. We continue to update and release new content as the ever-changing industry continues to evolve. </p> <p> As demand for skilled Android developers increases in the job marketplace, there is an even greater need for educators to train the next generation of Android developers. That is why we created these resources to help support and empower educators. </p> <p> <strong>New Android Development with Kotlin instructor-led curriculum</strong> </p> <p> Today we‚Äôre announcing the launch of our new instructor-led curriculum for<a href=\"http://d.android.com/teach\"> Android Development with Kotlin</a>. This is for classroom learning (virtual or in-person) with an instructor delivering lectures on important Android concepts, and students receiving hands-on practice through codelabs. The official course materials are now available and can be freely modified by instructors to adapt to their students‚Äô needs. </p> <p> This is a major update to the curriculum we released in 2018. The updates account for the most recent changes in the Android platform, from the release of the <a href=\"http://d.android.com/jetpack\">Android Jetpack libraries</a> to Android development becoming Kotlin-first. The <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/kotlin\">Kotlin programming language</a> helps developers become more productive with more concise syntax and improved code safety. Over 60% of professional Android developers already use Kotlin, and it‚Äôs Google‚Äôs recommended programming language for new developers building Android apps. While instructors do not need Android or Kotlin experience to teach the curriculum, prior programming experience is recommended. </p> <p> We‚Äôve partnered with universities and skilling partners in India such as Shivaji University, I. K. Gujral Punjab Technical University, Chandigarh University, Ganpat University, Telangana Academy for Skill and Knowledge (TASK), and Information and Communication Technology Academy of Kerala, who will be some of the first to offer this curriculum to their students in the Spring, with more universities to follow in the Fall and coming semesters. With the curriculum now available publicly, educators are welcome to start teaching Android development. </p> <p> <em>‚ÄúAs it‚Äôs mostly a hands-on course, students learn implementations which helps them in their placements in Mobile app companies.‚Äù -Dr. Kavita S. Oza, Shivaji University</em> </p> <p> <strong>Android Study Jams content now available for all developers</strong> </p> <p> Outside a formal classroom, learning in a peer group has also been shown as an effective way to learn Android. That is why we‚Äôre also making the<a href=\"http://d.android.com/teach#for-facilitators-leading-a-community-group\"> Android Study Jams program</a> available to all developers today. Android Study Jams enables a group of people to come together and learn Android development through hands-on codelabs in an online curriculum. An instructor is not needed to deliver lectures, but it is recommended to have a facilitator to organize the group meetings. No programming experience is needed to get started. Over 38,000 students in Google Developer Student Clubs around the globe have already participated in this program. </p> <p> <em>‚ÄúIntroducing people to Kotlin and being by their side at this first step which could touch their lives created great happiness and excitement for us.‚Äù - Ceren Tunay and Serkan Alc, Developer Student Club Turkey</em> </p> <p> With many paths to learning, it is always interesting to see the different journeys of students who become Android developers, and exciting to see the resulting personal success, innovative apps, and entrepreneurial pursuits they have. The following video highlights two developers and how learning Android development has shaped their careers. </p> \n  <center>\n   <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/DZ-rEgAWFkQ\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe>\n  </center> <p> For more details on these new offerings, check out the <a href=\"http://d.android.com/teach\">Android Development Resources for Educators</a>. </p> <p> For independent learners, we also offer <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/kotlin/campaign/learn\">self-paced learning content</a>, <a href=\"https://www.udacity.com/courses/all?skill=Android&amp;skill=Android+Development\">Udacity courses and Nanodegrees</a>, <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/user/androiddevelopers\">YouTube videos</a>, and more resources on <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide\">developer.android.com</a>. 12:52:23","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:52:23","title":"High Performance Game Audio with Oboe","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/F6CPWiWIrHs/high-performance-game-audio-with-oboe.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-X2RRLRFr0ZA/YFjP1ccU1wI/AAAAAAAAQRs/YyLABCxLVp0BUUHKg_onEYEDEcyXtHawQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-high-performance-game-audio-with-oboe-header.png\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-X2RRLRFr0ZA/YFjP1ccU1wI/AAAAAAAAQRs/YyLABCxLVp0BUUHKg_onEYEDEcyXtHawQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-high-performance-game-audio-with-oboe-header.png\"> <p><em>Posted by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/dagalpin?lang=en\">Dan Galpin</a> </em><p> \n    <center> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-X2RRLRFr0ZA/YFjP1ccU1wI/AAAAAAAAQRs/YyLABCxLVp0BUUHKg_onEYEDEcyXtHawQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-high-performance-game-audio-with-oboe-header.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"High Performance Game Audio with Oboe graphic\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"968\" data-original-width=\"3250\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-X2RRLRFr0ZA/YFjP1ccU1wI/AAAAAAAAQRs/YyLABCxLVp0BUUHKg_onEYEDEcyXtHawQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-high-performance-game-audio-with-oboe-header.png\" /></a>\n     </div> \n    </center> <p> <em> We've added the Oboe C++ audio library to the Android Game SDK. Oboe's support of high-performance, low-latency audio across the widest range of Android devices is the right choice for most game developers.</em> </p> <p> <strong><em>Single API</em></strong> </p> <p> <em>On Android devices running Android 8.1 (API level 27) and higher, Oboe takes advantage of the improved performance and features of AAudio while maintaining backward compatibility (using OpenSL ES) with Android 4.1 (API level 16) and higher. Oboe also adds key features on top of the platform APIs to improve the audio developer experience, such as resampling, format conversion, and dynamic latency tuning. It performs audio data transformations, such as channel count conversion, when necessary to improve performance on selected devices, and has workarounds for other device-specific behaviors that improve the robustness of your audio code. In short, Oboe is now the recommended way to write audio code in C/C++ on Android.</em> </p> <p> <strong><em>Integrating Oboe</em></strong> </p> <p> There are two primary ways to incorporate Oboe library prebuilts into your project. If you're using the Android Gradle plugin version 4.1.0 or higher along with CMake, and are using or can enable shared STL, enabling Oboe is as easy as adding Oboe to your Gradle dependencies, enabling prefabs, and adding a few lines to your CMakeLists file. </p> <p> You can also integrate Oboe by statically linking using the Android Game SDK. Begin by <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/games/sdk#download\">downloading the library</a> and checking it into your source control system. You need to be using minSdkVersion of 16 or higher with NDK release 18 or higher. Then, to specify the version of the game SDK to link in that's been compiled for the given ABI, API level, NDK, and STL combination, add a compiler include path in this form: </p> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">gamesdk/libs/[architecture]_API[apiLevel]_NDK[ndkVersion]_[stlVersion]_Release\nExample: gamesdk/libs/arm64-v8a_API24_NDK18_cpp_static_Release</pre> <p> Then add <code>-loboe_static</code> to your linker command. Since you don't need to bundle the liboboe.so shared library, static linking gives you a smaller code footprint. If the ABI, API level, NDK, and STL combination doesn't have a precompiled version available for your settings, you can alternately link against the shared library. We have more guidance, including how to configure CMake for static libraries, in our <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/games/sdk/oboe/update-build-settings\">developer documentation</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Oboe Basics</strong> </p> <p> To output audio, you begin by creating a stream with the required properties, including a callback that is used when the stream requires new data. </p> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">oboe::AudioStreamBuilder builder;\nbuilder.setPerformanceMode(oboe::PerformanceMode::LowLatency)\n  -&gt;setSharingMode(oboe::SharingMode::Exclusive)\n  -&gt;setDataCallback(myCallback)\n  -&gt;setFormat(oboe::AudioFormat::Float);</pre> <p> You'll then populate the audio data inside of the callback. If the stream creates successfully, that means you got the requested stream type. If you didn't specify these types, you'll have to query to see what format was returned. </p> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">class MyCallback : public oboe::AudioStreamDataCallback {\npublic:\n    oboe::DataCallbackResult\n    onAudioReady(oboe::AudioStream *audioStream, void *audioData, int32_t numFrames) {\n        // We requested AudioFormat::Float\n        auto *outputData = static_cast&lt;float *&gt;(audioData);\n        // TODO: populate audioData here\n        return oboe::DataCallbackResult::Continue;\n    }\n};</pre> <p> For full details on using Oboe, <em>check out the <a href=\"https://github.com/google/oboe/blob/master/docs/GettingStarted.md\">documentation</a>, <a href=\"https://github.com/google/oboe/tree/master/samples\">code samples</a> and <a href=\"https://google.github.io/oboe/reference/namespaceoboe.html\">API reference</a>. There's even <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/codelabs/musicalgame-using-oboe?hl=en#0\">a codelab</a> which shows you how to build a simple rhythm-based game.</em> </p> <p> <em>If you have any issues, please file them <a href=\"https://github.com/google/oboe/issues\">here</a>. We'd love to hear from you.</em> </p>\n    <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n     <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?a=F6CPWiWIrHs:30ACUc6jYMg:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Header image with text saying Android Dev Journey\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"969\" data-original-width=\"3244\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-8ovUAQdPOG8/YBSJkS0x93I/AAAAAAAAQCw/LV9Uos1w5AYwtqAK-CdZBNp76QtdNJFhwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_WrapUp_Blog_Jan.jpg\" /></a>\n  </div> <p>We kicked off the #AndroidDevJourney to give members of our community the opportunity to share their stories through our social platforms. Each Saturday from January through June we‚Äôll feature a new developer on <a href=\"https://twitter.com/AndroidDev\">our Twitter account</a>. We have received an overwhelming number of inspirational stories and hope you enjoy reading through the ones we‚Äôve selected below. </p> <p> For a chance to be featured in our February spotlight series, tweet us your story using #AndroidDevJourney. </p> \n  <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n   <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-x_gyRQ5wQ4E/YBRxzJ8i6oI/AAAAAAAAQBc/RvdLteCWg4E6p7DA7mdgPJnGhJfL0RUKwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B2.jpg\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Head shot of Niharika Arora\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"1200\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-x_gyRQ5wQ4E/YBRxzJ8i6oI/AAAAAAAAQBc/RvdLteCWg4E6p7DA7mdgPJnGhJfL0RUKwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B2.jpg\" /></a>\n  </div> <h2>Niharika Arora</h2> <p> <strong>Tell me about your journey in becoming an Android Developer and how you got started.</strong> </p> <p> <em>My journey started in the field of Android when I was in my 4th year of undergrad studies. I got an internship in a startup named GreenAppleSolutions. There I got a chance to work on an Android project from scratch and luckily my first project went live on the Play Store. During this whole internship, I found Android so interesting because everything you code, you can see the results live in front of you on your device. I started loving Android and decided to take Android as my career path.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What‚Äôs one shortcut, tip, or hack you can‚Äôt live without?</strong> </p> <p> <em>I am a big fan of Android Lint, which has saved me many times from manually finding deprecated calls/APIs. It has also helped me in following the best practices and making my code more optimized, secure, and highly performant. </em> </p> <p> <strong>What's the one piece of advice you wish someone would have given you when you started on your journey?</strong> </p> <p> <em>Actually, there are two, </em> </p> \n  <ul> \n   <li><em>Clearing a small doubt is equally as important even if you think that is a stupid one. Ask as many queries as you can till the time you are satisfied with the answer. </em> <li><em>Reading tutorials is good, but start exploring the documentations in depth. Initially, it might look too much to start with, but it will build you up to be a good developer in the long run.</em></li></li>\n  </ul> \n  <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n   <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-WOBeqgC2VKw/YBRywbBCgKI/AAAAAAAAQBo/UCdBJV5F4d0gOQHiaSTTRrPj34TE0mOywCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B3.jpg\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Head shot of Walmyr Carvalho\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"1200\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-WOBeqgC2VKw/YBRywbBCgKI/AAAAAAAAQBo/UCdBJV5F4d0gOQHiaSTTRrPj34TE0mOywCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B3.jpg\" /></a>\n  </div> <h2>Walmyr Carvalho</h2> <p> <strong>Tell me about your journey in becoming an Android Developer and how you got started.</strong> </p> <p><em>Funny thing! I started working with mobile on iOS, in 2010, but then in 2011 my college final project was an app for civil construction and nobody on the team had a Mac, so we did it for Android (We got a 10, btw!)! At that time I was teaching technology to some government people and wasn‚Äôt into coding that much, but then after project in 2011 I got my first job as Junior Android Developer and it got me so hooked on the platform that I couldn‚Äôt leave!</em></p> <p><em>I was able to work with Java on Eclipse + ADT, Holo, ActionBarSherlock, the beginnings of Material Design and was attending Google I/O ‚Äô13 when Google announced Android Studio, which was a very humbling but insightful experience to me, not only because of the learning but also the people I met that helped me a lot as well!</em></p> <p><em>Since then, I‚Äôve been working with mobile and, mostly, with Android for more than 10 years now, helping a lot of Brazilian tech companies and unicorns with their Android projects and since 2016 I‚Äôm one of the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/programs/experts/directory/\">Google Developer Experts</a> for Android around here.</em></p> <p><em>Also, I love development and design communities, so I try to be involved with that as much as I can. I‚Äôm a former organizer of <a href=\"http://meetup.com/gdg-sp\">GDG S√£o Paulo</a> and the creator and organizer of <a href=\"http://meetup.com/kotlin-meetup-sp\">Kotlin Meetup S√£o Paulo</a> and <a href=\"http://androiddevbr.org/\">Android Dev BR</a> - the biggest brazilian/lusophone Android community in the world, with more than 7.500 members! </em></p> <p><em>Lastly, I‚Äôm also involved with the national startup community, as a mentor for <a href=\"https://acestartups.com.br/startups/\">ACE Startups</a> and <a href=\"https://www.campus.co/google-for-startups-accelerator-global/\">Google For Startups Accelerator</a> programs in Brazil. </em></p> <p> <strong>What‚Äôs one Android development shortcut, tip, or hack you can‚Äôt live without?</strong> </p> <p><em> There‚Äôs a simple but powerful shortcut on Android Studio that I use a lot, which is the multi-cursor occurrence selection, which can be achieved using Ctrl + G (macOS) / Alt + J (Windows + Linux) for incremental occurrences selection and/or Ctrl + Cmd + G / Shift + Ctrl + Alt + J to select all occurrences once. Seems silly, but this shortcut helps me so much to get going on my code, especially when it comes to refactoring. I use it everyday! </em></p> <p> <strong>What's the one piece of advice you wish someone would have given you when you started on your journey?</strong> </p> <p> <p><em>I think I would resume my advice in two words: learn and share. </em><p> <p><em>Learn as much as you can, not only with the amazing content available on official documentation, and from the community, but also learn from your own mistakes through consistent practice. There‚Äôs a lot of content available for free on the internet, and also both Google and GDEs (Google Developer Experts) like me can get you going, so keep practicing and get your knowledge online!</em></p> <p><em>And once you learn, share with other people! If I‚Äôm where I am today is because I was able to share what I couldn‚Äôt find when I was learning, so please, share your knowledge! The Android community is amazing and super helpful, you can reach literally the creators of the APIs and libraries you use on Twitter, Reddit and many other places. Write an article, record a podcast or a video, there are many formats that you could use.</em></p> <p><em>The internet is such a powerful tool for learning and sharing and I really recommend you to do that there, and I‚Äôm definitely here to help if needed! :)</em></p> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-lWSEOZ8vXzU/YBR0cyExqDI/AAAAAAAAQB0/aqvS3kp0KiAPcrr2FwQEs00-DArz1A6rQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B4.jpg\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Head shot of Nate Washington\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"1200\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-lWSEOZ8vXzU/YBR0cyExqDI/AAAAAAAAQB0/aqvS3kp0KiAPcrr2FwQEs00-DArz1A6rQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B4.jpg\" /></a>\n     </div> <h2>Nate Washington</h2> <p> <strong><em>Tell me about your journey in becoming an Android Developer and how you got started.</em></strong> </p> <p><em>I became an Android developer in 2015, while working on my first business idea. I couldn‚Äôt afford to go back to school, so I decided to try my hand at starting a business instead. I launched a web application, but my customers insisted on having a native app for their needs as well. I originally looked for someone with more experience, but ultimately decided to just teach myself how to build an Android app. Fast forward to 2017, and my cofounder Christian and I launched the Android app for our company, <a href=\"https://qoins.io/\">Qoins</a>, on the Google Play Store. Since then, we‚Äôve served tens of thousands of Android customers and raised a few rounds of funding.</em></p> <p> <strong>What‚Äôs one Android development shortcut, tip, or hack you can‚Äôt live without?<em> </em></strong> </p> <p> <em>Being able to test my Android builds on virtual devices is a lifesaver. There are a lot of different scenarios to account for when building Android apps for thousands of different devices. Tools such as Firebase Test Labs, as well as other virtual device services allow me to create specific scenarios for hands-on testing that I can‚Äôt achieve with the physical Android devices that I own.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What's the one piece of advice you wish someone would have given you when you started on your journey? </strong> </p> <p> <em>Making mistakes is OK; it's all part of the process.</em> </p> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-mr5dRXCy_1o/YBR1GIkb1zI/AAAAAAAAQB8/Q5EBHMVSa6UKBv4AbPORoqrgbbx9XgsNQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B5.jpg\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Headshot of Yuki Anzai\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"1200\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-mr5dRXCy_1o/YBR1GIkb1zI/AAAAAAAAQB8/Q5EBHMVSa6UKBv4AbPORoqrgbbx9XgsNQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B5.jpg\" /></a>\n     </div> <h2>Yuki Anzai</h2> <p> <strong>Tell me about your journey in becoming an Android Developer and how you got started.</strong> </p> <p> <em>My journey began when I got my very first Android device, the HTC Magic, at Google Developer Day 2009. At that time, I was a college student and writing my personal application with JavaFX, so I had experience and familiarity with Java. Then I soon started to port my app to Android. After graduation I worked at a software company and wanted to develop Android apps as my job. But there seemed no opportunity at that company. So I created my own small company that is the agency to develop Android apps.</em> </p> <p> <strong> What‚Äôs one Android development shortcut, tip, or hack you can‚Äôt live without?</strong> </p> <p> <em>There are many. If I had to pick one, it would be Android Studio. I always appreciate the awesomeness of Android Studio because I started Android app development with Eclipse. (Also I can't live without Kotlin, RecyclerView, ConstraintLayout ...)</em> </p> <p> <em>The shortcut of Android Studio that I can't live without is Command + B ÔºàDeclaration or Usages. This allows us to jump between the declaration and usages. It's very useful to read source codes including Android platform and libraries codes.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What's the one piece of advice you wish someone would have given you when you started on your journey?</strong> </p> <p> <em>Read official documents. Read source codes of platform, libraries that you use. One of the ways to accelerate learning is to create an app through first to end (until release to the market).</em> </p> <p> <em>Don't rely on libraries too much especially that affect the whole structure of your app. Your app might live longer than libraries.</em> </p> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-IpuLc93kvTo/YBR1hmAx43I/AAAAAAAAQCE/K8UQUC6qndEnx8lpURXPztyvrmdDYUKFACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B6.jpg\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Head shot of Madona Syombua\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"1200\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-IpuLc93kvTo/YBR1hmAx43I/AAAAAAAAQCE/K8UQUC6qndEnx8lpURXPztyvrmdDYUKFACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B6.jpg\" /></a>\n     </div> <h2>Madona Syombua</h2> <p> <strong>Tell me about your journey in becoming an Android Developer and how you got started.</strong> </p> <p> <em>My Android Journey started back in early 2014; before that, I worked as a junior Java developer for a small firm building inventory systems. However, that did not interest me, and I kept looking for something great to do with my Java knowledge. I bought my first phone, a Nokia, and saw apps in the phone and wondered how they made those apps. I researched and learned that apps were actually written in Java, and that's how my journey began. </em> </p> <p> <em>I recall building my first application, Simple Math, with only activities since fragments were not there; what an improvement we've had over the years. Simple Math had 500 downloads with a 4.5 rating, and this really motivated me to build more applications. I later won the Grow With Google Scholarship (2018), which boosted my career. During this one-year scholarship, I launched my second application, <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.madonasyombua.budgetbuddy&amp;hl=en_US&amp;gl=US\">Budgeting Buddy</a>, on the Google Play Store and has a 4.5 rating with over five thousand downloads. I currently work for Streem as an Android Engineer, and I indeed love how far Android has come and how the technology and maintenance have improved over the years. Especially the Emulator. </em> </p> <p> <strong>What's one Android development shortcut, tip, or hack you can't live without. </strong> </p> <p> <em>A shortcut I can't live without is [options + Command + L ] and [Options + Command + O]; this really helps me during my pull request process. An amazing hack that I have learned to appreciate is the git local history option, WOW lifesaver. Sometimes you might forget what you had changed, but this hack always saves my life.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What's the one piece of advice you wish someone would have given you when you started on your journey? </strong> </p> <p> <em>Actually, when I transitioned into mobile completely, I felt the learning curve was something I would have to accommodate In my life, which has really helped me a lot. Always staying in front of the game by always learning what is new, what is being recommended, and why it is needed. For instance, having Room was an amazing advancement, now dagger Hilt, and many more. So if I can turn this around and advise new developers, be ready to learn and you will enjoy Android Development.</em> </p> <p> \n      <hr> \n      </hr></p> <p>The Android Developer community prides itself in its inclusivity and welcomes developers from all backgrounds and stages of life. A GDG meetup event includes talks on a wide range of technical topics where you can learn new skills through hands-on workshops. </p> \n     <center>\n      <p> Join a chapter near you <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/community/gdg/groups\">here</a>. </p>\n     </center> \n     <center>\n      <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n       <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ZmmknLJ_ZBE/YBR248DwllI/AAAAAAAAQCY/suDSAy5x7pYGceUq6-Hn0vA9eyqcMW_FACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B8.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:25%\" alt=\"Women Techmakers logo\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"122\" data-original-width=\"640\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ZmmknLJ_ZBE/YBR248DwllI/AAAAAAAAQCY/suDSAy5x7pYGceUq6-Hn0vA9eyqcMW_FACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B8.png\" /></a>\n      </div>\n     </center> <p> Founded in 2014, Google‚Äôs Women Techmakers is dedicated to helping all women thrive in tech through community, visibility and resources. "https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-qEAbLj4VjWM/YBR3qJ5XlSI/AAAAAAAAQCk/GXJDi7q9vZQFlUj79CZW6l0gRc4KzIBsACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B9.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn67@2020_3/2021/04/03/04-52-34-958_b661f8a8ece8f174.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn85@2020_6/2021/04/03/04-52-34-976_e6aa4d73b74f71ed.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?i=XLcUriodFYM:g3AfZuVOALk:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn60@2020_2/2021/04/03/04-52-35-529_08385d830851b8cd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~4/XLcUriodFYM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn72@2020_5/2021/04/03/04-52-35-529_aa2909476357b807.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617425543980},{"createdTime":"2021-04-03 12:52:23","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:52:23","title":"Low-Power Sleep Tracking on Android","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/aHtgBL8Qo7U/low-power-sleep-tracking-on-android.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-IS-fCBd29EM/YDfU6jz7UtI/AAAAAAAAQKg/Zv-ufO0TKwQYo9dIxwP2NgGFy4oxkWl8gCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-LowPowerSleepTracking-Social-v2%2B%25281%2529.png\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-IS-fCBd29EM/YDfU6jz7UtI/AAAAAAAAQKg/Zv-ufO0TKwQYo9dIxwP2NgGFy4oxkWl8gCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-LowPowerSleepTracking-Social-v2%2B%25281%2529.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Nick Grayson, Product Manager</em></p> \n  <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n   <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-zd0Y7AshEqI/YDUoxN3HWoI/AAAAAAAAQII/X6JfLtKrV2ofX6hXoMJszZCGYk-VCr-MACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-LowPowerSleepTracking-Header-v2.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Illustration of phone with moon and Android logo on screen\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"968\" data-original-width=\"3250\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-zd0Y7AshEqI/YDUoxN3HWoI/AAAAAAAAQII/X6JfLtKrV2ofX6hXoMJszZCGYk-VCr-MACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-LowPowerSleepTracking-Header-v2.png\" /></a>\n  </div> <p> Android works best when it helps developers create apps that people love. That‚Äôs why we are dedicated to providing useful APIs like <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/location-context/activity-recognition\">Activity Recognition</a> which, with the user‚Äôs permission, can detect user‚Äôs activities (such as whether a user is biking or walking) to help apps provide contextually aware experiences. </p> <p> So much of what we do relies on a good night's rest. Our phones have become great tools for making more informed decisions about our sleep. And by being informed about sleep habits, people can make better decisions throughout the day about sleep, which affects things like concentration and mental health. </p> <p> In an effort to help our users stay informed about their sleep, we are making our Sleep API publicly available. </p> <h2>What is the Sleep API?</h2> <p> The Sleep API is an Android Activity Recognition API that surfaces information about the user‚Äôs sleep. It can be used to power features like the <a href=\"https://blog.google/outreach-initiatives/digital-wellbeing/improve-your-sleep/\">Bedtime mode in Clock</a>. </p> <p> This sleeping information is reported in two ways: </p> \n  <ol> \n   <li>A ‚Äòsleep confidence‚Äô, which is reported at a regular interval (up to 10 minutes) <li>A daily sleep segment which is reported after a wakeup is detected </li> </li>\n  </ol> <p> The API uses an on-device artificial intelligence model that uses the device‚Äôs light and motion sensors as inputs. </p> <p> As with all of our Activity Recognition APIs, the app must be granted the Physical Activity Recognition runtime permission from the user to detect sleep. </p> <h2>Why is this important for developers?</h2> <p> Developers spend valuable engineering time to combine sensor signals to determine when the user has started or ended activities like sleep. These detection algorithms are inconsistent between apps and when multiple apps independently and continuously check for changes in user activity, battery life suffers. </p> <p> The Sleep API is a simple API that centralizes sleep detection processing in a battery-efficient manner. For this launch, we are proud to collaborate with Urbandroid, the developer of the popular alarm app, <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.urbandroid.sleep&amp;hl=en_US&amp;gl=US\">Sleep As Android</a> </p> \n  <div> \n   <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4uX0okdxdFk/YDUpibS2ZbI/AAAAAAAAQIQ/u_EpNo3KYvso4iu9cQhXfXQHQ9u63VETQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ic_launcher.1024.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img id=\"floatLeft\" style=\"width:30%; padding:0 1em 1em 0;\" alt=\"Android logo sleeping\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"225\" data-original-width=\"225\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4uX0okdxdFk/YDUpibS2ZbI/AAAAAAAAQIQ/u_EpNo3KYvso4iu9cQhXfXQHQ9u63VETQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ic_launcher.1024.png\" /></a> \n   <blockquote>\n    <em>Sleep as Android is a swiss army knife for getting a better night‚Äôs rest. It tracks sleep duration, regularity, phases, snoring, and more. Sleep Duration is one of the most important parameters to watch for ensuring a good night‚Äôs rest. The new Sleep API gives us a fantastic opportunity to track it automatically in the most battery efficient way imaginable.</em> \n    <p>- Sleep as Android Team</p> \n   </blockquote> \n  </div> <br><br> <h2>When can I start using this API?</h2> <p> The Sleep API is available for developers to use now as part of the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/android/guides/releases#febuary_18_2021\">latest version of Google Play Services</a>. </p> <p> This API is one step of our efforts to help our users get a better night's rest. We look forward to working more on this API and in this area in the future. </p> <p> If you are interested in exploring or using this API, check out our <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/location-context/sleep\">API Documentation</a>. </p>\n    <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n     <a src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-q-qKHM6GpZg/YDlQ0-FBECI/AAAAAAAAQK8/cd6dYiywVtw19lxgx1xhtQzTrqy2yKPPwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_WrapUp_Blog_Feb.jpg\" /></a>\n  </div> <p>Our second edition of #AndroidDevJourney is here! At the beginning of this year we launched the #AndroidDevJourney to share the stories of members of our community through our social platforms. Each Saturday, from January through June, we‚Äôll feature a new developer on <a href=\"https://twitter.com/AndroidDev\">our Twitter account</a>.</p> <p>For a chance to be featured in our March spotlight series, tweet us your story using #AndroidDevJourney.</p> \n  <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n   <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/--Y7BH2rXpuQ/YDlR1Erk5DI/AAAAAAAAQLE/TRDYaRVnB24RbvJnobo9Ci_YjU9wf2nRwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Kelly.jpg\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Andrew Kelly\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"1200\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/--Y7BH2rXpuQ/YDlR1Erk5DI/AAAAAAAAQLE/TRDYaRVnB24RbvJnobo9Ci_YjU9wf2nRwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Kelly.jpg\" /></a>\n  </div> <h2>Andrew Kelly</h2> <p> <strong>Tell me about your journey to becoming an Android Developer and how you got started.</strong> </p> <p> <em>In 2012 I was working as a contractor for the NSW government here in Australia as a Java J2EE web developer. I'd been in that role for 11 years, building web apps for students and teachers. However, in 2012 the government decided that contractors were expensive and let us all go. So while in my hand-over period I'd read about some kids who were writing Android apps and making lots of money doing so. The Android Market was new and so any app uploaded got a large audience, and since I already knew Java it seemed like switching from a web developer to a mobile developer might be a smart career move. So I purchased a new phone, the HTC Legend and spent the next 2 weeks learning everything I could about Android apps. It was the first time I could run software I'd written on a device made by someone else that I could carry around with me. It was a very exciting time where any app idea seemed possible.</em> </p> <p> <em> When my contract finally ended, I managed to get a new job working for a mobile development agency and started working on Android apps for their clients. In order to learn more about Android app development, I started to attend the local Android meetups and Google Developer Group events, listening to speakers (mostly from Google) and trying to improve my skills as an Android developer.</em> </p> <p> <em> In 2013 I was offered the opportunity to become the organiser of the Sydney GDG and it was that year that I also attended my first Google I/O (I've been every year since). One of the hard parts about being a GDG organiser is finding speakers, so occasionally if there were no speakers, or if a speaker dropped out at the last minute, I would step in and give a talk instead. 2013 was also the year I decided to move on from the mobile agency I was working at, and I spent the next 5 years working as a freelance contractor, working with clients such as eBay, the Sydney Opera House, and one of the large banks in Australia. Being the organiser of GDG Sydney and a regular speaker at the meetups meant finding work was quite easy.</em> </p> <p> <em> In 2016 because of all the speaking I was doing I was approached to join the Google Developer Experts program, at this time I was doing regular talks at both the GDG Sydney and Android meetup events every couple of months. When I joined the GDE program, I handed over my GDG responsibilities to some friends, who still run it to this day. As part of the GDE program I've been lucky enough to attend many Google I/O events, and I've also had the opportunity to speak at conferences all over the world, including DroidCon Boston, Mobile Era in Oslo, DevFest Melbourne, DroidCon Singapore, Chicago Roboto and many others. Having the chance to speak to so many people all over the world has been very rewarding, and I've made many friends.</em> </p> <p> <em> In 2019 I joined the company where I work today - mx51, I'm the lead Android developer designing and building apps that run on payment terminals, which also integrate with Point of Sales systems. I'm still a GDE but with the 2020 madness the ability to speak at in-person events was severely hindered. I hope that in-person events will start again soon and that I can continue my journey as a GDE.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What‚Äôs one shortcut, tip, or hack you can‚Äôt live without?</strong> </p> <p> <em>Android development is constantly changing and advancing, so there is always something new to learn. My tip would be to always be learning, there are lots of ways to do this, subscribe to the <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVHFbqXqoYvEWM1Ddxl0QDg\">Android Developers YouTube channels</a> and <a href=\"https://medium.com/androiddevelopers\">Medium publications</a>. Follow Googlers and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/googledevexpert\">Google Developer Experts</a> on Twitter for new tips and posts. Subscribe to the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/subscribe\">Android Weekly newsletter</a> for an overview of new libraries and blog posts, and attend your local <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/community/gdg\">GDG chapter and Meetups</a>. Not only are these great ways to learn new aspects of Android development, but with meetups they're a great place to meet other Android developers, share successes, and ask for advice on problems.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What's the one piece of advice you wish someone would have given you when you started on your journey?</strong> </p> <p> <em>When I started out as an Android developer, I could never have dreamed about being a Google Developer Expert, travelling the world and speaking at large events. It took me a long time to learn that it's ok not to know the answers to people's questions. If at an event someone asks something you don't know, it's ok to say so. You can always say that you'll find out later and get back to them. There is no need to make up a wrong answer on the spot and lead someone off course. People are often scared that a topic they're presenting might not be the best or greatest way to do something, and they fear looking stupid. If a person in the audience suggests a better way that shouldn't be a worry, 1) you learnt something, 2) everyone else learnt something and 3) there may be scenarios where your solution is better and a discussion can be had. So my advice would be, when speaking don't fear questions but embrace the opportunity to help someone immediately, or later, or perhaps discover something new yourself.</em> </p> \n  <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n   <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-mO2K76oUO_k/YDlS3oLBHFI/AAAAAAAAQLM/oNLQdR61aYEdu_D3ewtafLAKmc0v5Zw3QCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Dominguez.jpg\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Amanda Hinchman-Dominguez\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"1200\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-mO2K76oUO_k/YDlS3oLBHFI/AAAAAAAAQLM/oNLQdR61aYEdu_D3ewtafLAKmc0v5Zw3QCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Dominguez.jpg\" /></a>\n  </div> <h2>Amanda Hinchman-Dominguez</h2> <p> <strong>Tell me about your journey to becoming an Android Developer and how you got started.</strong> </p> <p> <em>I dabbled in Android development in college with the student mobile development group, but it wasn't until I was a few years in web development I made the real switch over. Back in my web dev days, I joined the Kotlin community, where I felt immediately welcome. Shortly after, I moved to Chicago a few years back when I heard there was a Kotlin community in the tech scene. </em> </p> <p> <em>Getting up to speed with Android at a professional level is a whole different game, and I've been lucky to find the overlapping Kotlin/Android community both locally and globally. Android development has accelerated my career technically and professionally, yet the world is so deep and vast within the sandbox of Android development. </em> </p> <p> <em>Already being an active enthusiast with Kotlin, it only felt natural to switch to Android, and I've never looked back. Since then, I've been working scalable and complex Android applications, and contributing with some technical writing along the way. I'm currently co-writing with my colleague, Pierre Laurence, on ‚ÄúProgramming Android with Kotlin: Achieving Structured Concurrency with Coroutines with O'Reilly‚Äù, and I'm excited to have it come out sometime this year.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What‚Äôs one shortcut, tip, or hack you can‚Äôt live without?</strong> </p> <p> <em>For larger projects, it's sometimes hard to locate the file you're looking at in your Project view. You can use the target symbol ‚äï to get a highlight the file you're currently on in Android Studio. </em> </p> \n  <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n   <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-gaPrtvlOMWQ/YDlUAuObVMI/AAAAAAAAQLU/SydZMDMHcswviHtNUms9oLKdnTF91DFkgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-02-03%2Bat%2B12.44.20%2BPM.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Android Studio interface with arrows pointing to target symbol\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"859\" data-original-width=\"1600\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-gaPrtvlOMWQ/YDlUAuObVMI/AAAAAAAAQLU/SydZMDMHcswviHtNUms9oLKdnTF91DFkgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-02-03%2Bat%2B12.44.20%2BPM.png\" /></a>\n  </div> <p> <strong>What's the one piece of advice you wish someone would have given you when you started on your journey?</strong> </p> <p> <em>Only install LeakCanary when, and only when, you <strong>and</strong> your team is ready for that conversation üòÅ</em> </p> \n  <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n   <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-GsVaOMDCKrM/YDlUZUEljBI/AAAAAAAAQLc/OnDbJMGwSfM2GGLjsuIVu2S5F5oUy8nBgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Edwards.jpg\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Anthony Edwards JR\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"1200\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-GsVaOMDCKrM/YDlUZUEljBI/AAAAAAAAQLc/OnDbJMGwSfM2GGLjsuIVu2S5F5oUy8nBgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Edwards.jpg\" /></a>\n  </div> <h2>Anthony Edwards Jr</h2> <p> <strong>Tell me about your journey to becoming an Android Developer and how you got started.</strong> </p> <p> <em>My journey as a developer started as a child. As a kid, I was obsessed with robots. I remember my dad bought me a Lego set called Lego Mindstorm, which was basically a robotics set with sensors and motors, plus it was also programmable. After graduating high school, I enrolled in the US Army as an Aviation Maintenance Repairer. After 6 years, I was honorably discharged then enrolled in college at Fordham University. In 2014, I received a Bachelor of Science in Computer Science. About 2 years later, I met my now wife, and together we started building EatOkra as a way for us to find black-owned restaurants in Brooklyn, NY. As we introduced the application to new people, they shared it with their network; before we knew it, many people were asking us to cover more areas in the south. </em> </p> <p> <strong>What‚Äôs one shortcut, tip, or hack you can‚Äôt live without?</strong> </p> <p> <em>Learn how to ask the right questions.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What's the one piece of advice you wish someone would have given you when you started on your journey?</strong> </p> <p> <em>One piece of advice I wish I took more seriously was to not build an application using beta technology. EatOkra's MVP was created using a beta version of a software framework. It started out good but then as they made updates, at times, I ended up having to wait months for certain issues to get fixed. I also had to completely stop and restart the app with an entirely new code base because the company decided to change how they architected the code. I learned a lot but it was painful to navigate.</em> </p> \n  <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n   <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-td813uopMIE/YDlUqo_4hgI/AAAAAAAAQLk/-iKYaBmZBxMdBfKx9MyVaU74eitVRhChwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_-Tovar.jpg\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Dinorah Tovar\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"1200\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-td813uopMIE/YDlUqo_4hgI/AAAAAAAAQLk/-iKYaBmZBxMdBfKx9MyVaU74eitVRhChwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_-Tovar.jpg\" /></a>\n  </div> <h2>Dinorah Tovar</h2> <p> <strong>Tell me about your journey to becoming an Android Developer and how you got started.</strong> </p> <p> <em>My journey started a couple of years ago (I was still in college) when I saw the Android Developer Udacity course. There was no nano degree back in the day. So once I saw it, I started building some apps for myself. From there, I applied for my first job as a junior developer in a big consulting firm. Then I started seeing more courses and started following a lot of people at Twitter, like Sam Edwards and Joe Birch (both GDE). The community made me grow and learn. A couple of years later I got my first team and I began delivering speeches at conferences and keeping up my Medium blog on the side. The community offers me feedback and knowledge, and especially a place to learn. My first conference was with WomenWhoCode.org here in Mexico. They opened a place for me without any experience. The same happened with Google Developers Groups here in Mexico City. </em> </p> <p> <em>I became a Lead Engineer during my second job and I began doing worldwide conferences. I asked for feedback from Sam Edwards and Carlos Mu√±oz (also GDEs in Colombia) and they told me not to worry because I would amazingly and they encouraged me to keep doing it. </em> </p> <p> <em>I got a really nice offer to start from scratch here as a Mobile Platform engineer in Mexico City with a huge fintech Startup (Konfio.mx). This is my current job, which means I am in the architectural office where we choose new ideas and new processes and pretty much service all the areas in the company.</em> </p> <p> <em>I started creating a group of series to teach people some specific topics that I noticed were not deeply addressed. I also started getting involved in Kotlin Multiplatform and then I was reached out to by two GDE that nominated me to become GDE, Walmyr Carvalho, and Sam Edwards. They offered me feedback about my latest talks, podcast, and series and I was accepted at the end of 2020. Right now, I'm trying to learn more and deliver more talks and blog posts to the community.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What‚Äôs one shortcut, tip, or hack you can‚Äôt live without?</strong> </p> <p> <em>My special hack as an Android Developer is to use Wireless Debugging in the lastest Android Studio for physical devices. It is my favorite part because I don't need to use any cables and the setup is super easy!</em> </p> <p> <strong>What's the one piece of advice you wish someone would have given you when you started on your journey?</strong> </p> <p> <em>My advice is that learning is a process, things change and all of this must be welcome because we are addressing the evolution of the platform as we code. Also, read everything you can because people in the community are amazing and they love to teach! Open an account on Twitter, because there are a lot of people giving tips in less than 180 characters. </em> </p> \n  <hr> \n   <p>The Android Developer community prides itself in its inclusivity and welcomes developers from all backgrounds and stages of life. If you‚Äôre feeling inspired and want to learn more about how to become a part of our community, here are a few resources to help get you started. </p> \n   <center>\n    <p> <em>Dive into <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/\">developer.android.com</a></em> </p>\n   </center> \n   <center>\n    <p> <em>Follow us on <a href=\"https://twitter.com/AndroidDev\">Twitter</a></em> </p>\n   </center> \n   <center>\n    <p> <em>Subscribe to our <a href=\"https://goo.gle/subscribe-androiddev-yt\">YouTube channel</a></em> </p>\n   </center> \n   <center>\n    <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-YvLu6Iqq3qY/YBR2PWa7aAI/AAAAAAAAQCQ/dViPshDrn2M6ekELBHImIGvn5D9zRsECwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B7.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:25%\" alt=\"GDG logo\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"810\" data-original-width=\"1440\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-YvLu6Iqq3qY/YBR2PWa7aAI/AAAAAAAAQCQ/dViPshDrn2M6ekELBHImIGvn5D9zRsECwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B7.png\" /></a>\n    </div>\n   </center> \n   <p> The Google Developer Groups program gives developers the opportunity to meet local developers with similar interests in technology. ","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/ywEhT974TuU/boosting-dev-success.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-AVwnqEsxp7Y/YEwHMnaKYkI/AAAAAAAAQPk/XB6r-ApAW9oHD78jB4P8JejVYbjLDKnEACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/play%2Blogo.png\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-AVwnqEsxp7Y/YEwHMnaKYkI/AAAAAAAAQPk/XB6r-ApAW9oHD78jB4P8JejVYbjLDKnEACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/play%2Blogo.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Sameer Samat, VP, Product Management</em><p> <p> Helping developers build sustainable businesses is a core part of Google Play‚Äôs mission. We work with partners every day to understand the challenges they face and help them bring their innovative ideas to life. Getting a new app off the ground and into orbit is not easy! To aid their quest for growth we provide a broad range of support, from powerful <a href=\"https://play.google.com/console/about/grow-your-audience/\">marketing tools</a> and <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/03/google-play-console-powers-better.html\">actionable data in the Play Console</a>, education via <a href=\"https://playacademy.exceedlms.com/student/catalog\">Play Academy</a>,<a href=\"https://medium.com/googleplaydev\n\"> best practices</a> and <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/podcasts/apps-games-insights\">thought leadership</a> resources, programs such as the <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2020/07/the-winners-of-google-play-indie-games.html\">Indie Games Festival</a>, <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/editorial_collection/promotion_topic_b000054_games_indie_corner_tp?hl=en_GB&amp;gl=US\">Indie Corner</a>, and <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/community/accelerators\">accelerator programs</a> around the world. We‚Äôre always looking for new ways to give them an added boost. </p> <p> Starting on July 1, 2021 we are reducing the service fee Google Play receives when a developer sells digital goods or services to 15% for the first $1M (USD) of revenue every developer earns each year. With this change, 99% of developers globally that sell digital goods and services with Play will see a 50% reduction in fees. These are funds that can help developers scale up at a critical phase of their growth by hiring more engineers, adding to their marketing staff, increasing server capacity, and more. </p> <p> While these investments are most critical when developers are in the earlier stages of growth, scaling an app doesn‚Äôt stop once a partner has reached $1M in revenue ‚Äî we‚Äôve heard from our partners making $2M, $5M and even $10M a year that their services are still on a path to self-sustaining orbit. This is why we are making this reduced fee on the first $1M of total revenue earned each year available to every Play developer, regardless of size. We believe this is a fair approach that aligns with Google‚Äôs broader mission to help all developers succeed. We look forward to sharing full details in the coming months. </p> <p> As a platform we do not succeed unless our partners succeed. Android and Google Play have always listened to our developer partners from around the world and we continue to take their input into account as we build and run the ecosystem. We look forward to seeing more businesses scale to new heights on Android, and to further discussions with our developer community to find new ways to support them technically and economically as they build their businesses. </p>\n    <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n     <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?a=ywEhT974TuU:tyXo_Mihayk:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"480\" data-original-width=\"1600\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-xFLQ0zP3yeo/YGYmkWcHhYI/AAAAAAAAQTk/Nrk53fSAIises462o-RgP5rbZAe-XevyQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Untitled%2B%25282%2529.jpeg\" /></a>\n     </div>\n    </center> <p> In case you missed it, we‚Äôve just finished a <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NtpgWjiXEfg&amp;list=PLWz5rJ2EKKc_J88-h0PhCO_aV0HIAs9Qk\">MAD Skills series on WorkManager</a>. We started by introducing WorkManager for those new to the library and then proceeded to talk more about advanced usages including how to test and debug your WorkManager code. The series ended with an episode on how to migrate your old code from GCMNetworkManager and FirebaseJobDispatcher to use WorkManager instead. </p> <p> Here‚Äôs a quick summary of what we covered. </p> <h2>Episode 1: WorkManager: Basics</h2> <p> In our first episode, we explored the basics of WorkManager through the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/codelabs/android-workmanager\">WorkManager codelab</a>. We started by understanding how to define work we want done, and how to schedule the work. We then moved on to implementing different types of work: unique and periodic. Finally, we ended the episode by taking a look at <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/topic/performance/appstandby\">app standby buckets</a> to better understand how WorkManager schedules work. </p> <p> \n     <center> \n      <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/_SQM-10TB4k\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n     </center> <p> If you‚Äôre new to WorkManager, we also recommend taking a look at the following articles: </p> \n     <ul> \n      <li><a href=\"https://medium.com/androiddevelopers/introducing-workmanager-2083bcfc4712\">Introducing WorkManager</a> <li><a href=\"https://medium.com/androiddevelopers/workmanager-basics-beba51e94048\">WorkManager Basics</a> </li> </li>\n     </ul> <h2>Episode 2: WorkManager: Working in the background</h2> <p> The series continued with Ben giving a more in-depth look at how WorkManager deals with multi-threading. When working with threads, you have the option of using Executors, coroutines or RxJava, and Ben demonstrated each of these approaches with WorkManager. The episode concluded by demonstrating how to return a result when the work is completed so that the UI can be updated. </p> \n     <center> \n      <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/kpuMD2P7s5M\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n     </center> If you‚Äôre interested in using WorkManager with coroutines, we also recommend this article from Florina: <a href=\"https://medium.com/androiddevelopers/workmanager-kotlin-apis-a0fb9dfbfeb6\">WorkManager - Kotlin APIs</a> </p> <h2>Episode 3: WorkManager: Advanced configuration and testing</h2> <p> In episode 3, we took a look at how to customize the initialization of WorkManager and support apps that span multiple processes. We‚Äôve gotten a lot of questions from developers around testing and debugging, so Ben also dove into how to test your Workers, and useful debugging techniques. </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/nGtLtmZe6do\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <h2>Episode 4: Migrating from GCM NetworkManager and FirebaseJobDispatcher to WorkManager</h2> <p> In episode 4, we focused on how to migrate from old job scheduling libraries (GCMNetworkManager and FirebaseJobDispatcher) to WorkManager. Once your app starts targeting API level 30 and above, GCM NetworkManager and FirebaseJobDispatcher will no longer work on devices running Android Marshmallow (6.0) and above. If your app is still using either of those libraries, now is the time to update your apps to use WorkManager instead! </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/5siAia1sb8w\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe>\n    </center> <h2>Episode 5: WorkManager with Hugo</h2> <p> Android GDE <a href=\"https://twitter.com/botteaap\">Hugo Visser</a> talked about why he chose to use WorkManager in a health app he recently worked on and how the library has helped his development process. </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/CEUnCHnc5aA\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <h2>Episode 6: Live Q&amp;A</h2> <p> The series wrapped up with a live Q&amp;A session where we answered your WorkManager related questions. Watch the recording to see all your questions answered, including future plans for WorkManager, handling duplicate work, retrying failed work, and more! </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe For example, we added a new <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/androidx/car/app/model/GridTemplate\">GridTemplate</a>, which is useful when users rely primarily on images to make their selections. \n     <center> \n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-MLpA7kPaK4I/YDk5t4cv-PI/AAAAAAAAQK0/m_pIhXTAbgQWSwYODMpM0qdm8fYPU1nGgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-02-26%2Bat%2B1.06.08%2BPM.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-MLpA7kPaK4I/YDk5t4cv-PI/AAAAAAAAQK0/m_pIhXTAbgQWSwYODMpM0qdm8fYPU1nGgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-02-26%2Bat%2B1.06.08%2BPM.png\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n     </center> <p id=\"imgCaption\"> <em>Examples of the new GridTemplate in <code>androidx.car.app</code></em> </p> <p> On September 1, 2021, the closed source Android for Cars App Library (<code>com.google.android.libraries.car.app</code>) will no longer be available and the Google Play Store will not accept submissions that use <code>com.google.android.libraries.car.app</code>. Our development focus from now, including new features, is on <code>androidx.car.app</code>. We encourage you to migrate now and we‚Äôve created a <a href=\"https://developers.android.com/training/cars/jetpack-migration\">migration guide</a> that makes it easy. Migration usually takes less than a day, in our experience with early access partners. </p> <p> We‚Äôre working hard to stabilize <code>androidx.car.app</code> and prepare the Google Play Store for production submissions. 12:52:23","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:52:23","title":"Announcing Kotlin Symbol Processing (KSP) Alpha","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/_bhFw3V6MgI/announcing-kotlin-symbol-processing-ksp.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\" https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tl-oC11ymb0/YCLDMYK4v_I/AAAAAAAAQEM/C_qeIE53MZQTtRITP66rN83kwRIl_uEygCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/pasted%2Bimage%2B0%2B%252834%2529.png \"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tl-oC11ymb0/YCLDMYK4v_I/AAAAAAAAQEM/C_qeIE53MZQTtRITP66rN83kwRIl_uEygCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/pasted%2Bimage%2B0%2B%252834%2529.png \"> <p><em>Posted by <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/_bhFw3V6MgI/about:invalid#zSoyz\">Ting-Yuan Huang</a>‚Äé, Software Engineer and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/davidjwiner?lang=en\">David Winer</a>, Product Manager </em><p> \n    <center> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\"> \n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tl-oC11ymb0/YCLDMYK4v_I/AAAAAAAAQEM/C_qeIE53MZQTtRITP66rN83kwRIl_uEygCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/pasted%2Bimage%2B0%2B%252834%2529.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Android image\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"512\" data-original-width=\"1024\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tl-oC11ymb0/YCLDMYK4v_I/AAAAAAAAQEM/C_qeIE53MZQTtRITP66rN83kwRIl_uEygCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/pasted%2Bimage%2B0%2B%252834%2529.png\" /></a> \n     </div> \n    </center> <p> Today we are excited to announce the alpha of <strong>Kotlin Symbol Processing </strong>(KSP), an all-new tool for building lightweight compiler plugins in Kotlin. KSP offers similar functionality to <a href=\"https://kotlinlang.org/docs/reference/kapt.html\">KAPT</a>, however it‚Äôs up to 2x faster, offers direct access to Kotlin compiler features, and is being developed with multiplatform compatibility in mind. </p> <p> KSP is compatible with the Kotlin 1.4.30 release and onwards. You can check out the open source code and documentation in the <a href=\"http://goo.gle/ksp\">KSP GitHub repository</a>. </p> <h2>Why KSP?</h2> <p> The #1 request we hear from Kotlin developers is to make build speeds faster. Many developers iterate on and deploy apps dozens of times a day, so having to sit around waiting for a slow build can be very time consuming. One of the biggest challenges with compiling Kotlin code is that Kotlin doesn‚Äôt have a native annotation processing system. Annotation processors like <a href=\"http://d.android.com/room\">Room</a> are ubiquitous on Android and rely on Java annotation processing compatibility through the Kotlin Annotation Processing Tool (KAPT). KAPT can be slow to run, though, since it requires generating intermediate Java stubs that can then be ingested by the Java annotation processing system. </p> <p> When designing KSP, we thought about what annotation processing would look like for Kotlin if we built it from the ground up. KSP offers a powerful and yet simple API for parsing Kotlin code directly, dramatically reducing the build speed tax imposed by KAPT‚Äôs stub generation. Indeed, initial benchmarks with the Room library show that KSP is approximately 2x faster than KAPT. </p> <h2>Getting started</h2> <p> To see what KSP looks like in action, download the <a href=\"https://github.com/google/ksp/releases/download/1.4.30-1.0.0-alpha02/playground.zip\">KSP playground project</a> from GitHub. In it you‚Äôll find: </p> \n    <ul> \n     <li><strong>Library: </strong>A toy <code>test-processor</code> library that implements the builder pattern as a KSP processor <li><strong>Consuming project: </strong>A <code>workload</code> directory that shows how to use the builder processor in a real-world Kotlin project </li> </li> \n    </ul> <p> All of the logic for implementing the builder is in <code>test-processor</code> ‚Äî for the consumer (<code>workload</code>), the only difference between using KAPT and KSP is a two-line build file change: </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-WSEWZfQjV0w/YCLCf32fz4I/AAAAAAAAQEE/jz_02cOCV7kA4OzvSEknvLFDM_GE4x5_ACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-02-09%2Bat%2B12.11.52%2BPM.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-WSEWZfQjV0w/YCLCf32fz4I/AAAAAAAAQEE/jz_02cOCV7kA4OzvSEknvLFDM_GE4x5_ACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-02-09%2Bat%2B12.11.52%2BPM.png\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <p> This is the goal of KSP: most Android app developers don‚Äôt need to worry about its internals; other than this one line change, a library that supports KSP looks just like a normal annotation processor, only it‚Äôs up to 2x faster. That said, using KAPT and KSP in the same module will likely slow down your build initially, so during this alpha period, it is best to use KSP and KAPT in separate modules. </p> <p> As more annotation processors adopt KSP, we expect most of your modules to be able to use KSP as a near drop-in replacement for KAPT. For now, you can check out which annotation processors offer KSP support in <a href=\"https://github.com/google/ksp#supported-libraries\">this table</a>. If a library that supports or is&nbsp;implementing support for KSP is missing from the table, please submit a pull request with your suggestion! </p> <p> If you are an author of a library that currently uses annotation processing, you can find more information on how to make your library compatible with KSP in the <a href=\"https://github.com/google/ksp/blob/master/docs/quickstart.md\">quickstart</a> and <a href=\"https://github.com/google/ksp#how-ksp-looks-at-source-files\">README</a> guides. </p> <p> For library authors, now that KSP is in alpha, it‚Äôs a great time to start looking closely at it and giving us feedback on the API in the <a href=\"https://github.com/google/ksp/issues\">KSP issue tracker</a>. In addition, we regularly post release updates in the #ksp channel on <a href=\"https://surveys.jetbrains.com/s3/kotlin-slack-sign-up?_ga=2.48535333.2098599687.1609969960-1527966202.1605648568&amp;_gac=1.146918085.1607395508.CjwKCAiAwrf-BRA9EiwAUWwKXktnCOQy3WhM7Xq-xLGrdg9gTJK3LnofgXHZtq2PsbzL8O5j1uSw2hoC33wQAvD_BwE\">Kotlin Slack</a>. Since the developer preview last June, we‚Äôve closed over 100 bugs and issues, dozens of which have been reported by the amazing community of Kotlin library developers. </p> <p> <em>Java is a registered trademark of Oracle and/or its affiliates.</em> </p> \n    <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n     <a 12:52:23","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:52:23","title":"Google Play Console powers better strategic decisions with new engagement metrics and unique benchmarks ","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/-_INzOIq1Cg/google-play-console-powers-better.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-rWkGuip_YZE/YD5KIgm9lGI/AAAAAAAAQNk/O7k9AkpFLEUcccq09LGwN1-D1JL1DqWbQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/google-play-engagement-metrics-launch.png\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-rWkGuip_YZE/YD5KIgm9lGI/AAAAAAAAQNk/O7k9AkpFLEUcccq09LGwN1-D1JL1DqWbQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/google-play-engagement-metrics-launch.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Tom Grinsted, Product Manager, Google Play </em><p> <p> <strong>Today in Google Play Console, we‚Äôve launched a <a href=\"https://play.google.com/console/app/statistics?tab=COMPARE_TO_PEERS\">suite of new metrics*</a> and unique comparative benchmarks. Using these, you can evaluate your app or games‚Äô engagement and monetization trends against up to 250 different peersets, helping you make better, more informed decisions about your product roadmaps and opportunities.</strong> </p> <p> Whether you want to prioritize new features to drive engagement, experiment with pricing, or drive up retention, we hear from all developers that they need great data and insights to help make the best investments. </p> <p> While some larger developers can compare data from across their portfolios, this isn‚Äôt always possible ‚Äî for instance, when entering a new territory, if you don‚Äôt publish directly comparable apps, or if you only publish one or two games in the first place. In these types of cases, how do you know if your app or game‚Äôs performance is <em>good</em> and where you can be better? </p> <p> <strong>With this launch, we‚Äôre here to help all developers better contextualize and understand their performance. Here‚Äôs what‚Äôs new:</strong> </p> <p> <strong>New engagement and monetization metrics</strong> </p> <p> In partnership with experts in mobile apps and games growth, we‚Äôve introduced a new set of engagement and monetization metrics based on best practices in evaluating app and game performance. These include: </p> \n    <ul> \n     <li><strong>DAU/MAU</strong><br>The ratio of users who open your app each day vs. each month (28-day rolling period). This is a key measure of ‚Äústickiness.‚Äù It tells you if you‚Äôre driving regular, habitual use. <li><strong>28-day returning users</strong><br>The percentage of your daily users who have also used your app in the previous 28 days. This can help you judge if you‚Äôre building a loyal audience. <li><strong>DAU</strong> and <strong>MAU</strong> <strong>growth rates</strong><br>How quickly you‚Äôre growing the number of users who open your app daily and at least once in 28 days. These are your fundamental audience-growth measurements. <li><strong>ARPDAU<br /></strong>Average Revenue Per Daily Active User. This is your daily revenue divided by your DAU, which measures your success in driving revenue from your users. <li><strong>Average purchase value<br /></strong>How much you make on average from each transaction. This is useful for pricing optimization decisions. <li><strong>Purchases per buyer </strong>and <strong>User-buyer ratios<br /></strong>The number of times buyers transact with you, and the percentage of your DAUs and MAUs who become buyers. Especially helpful if you‚Äôre looking to see if there‚Äôs growth opportunity in increasing how many people purchase or how often. </li> </li></li></br></li></br></li></br></li>\n    </ul> <p> In total, we‚Äôre launching <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googleplay/android-developer/answer/139628#install\">15 new normalized metrics</a> with benchmarks, and making the absolute numerators and denominators available to query, too. They can all be found in the new ‚ÄúCompare to peers‚Äù tab in the <a href=\"https://play.google.com/console/app/statistics?tab=COMPARE_TO_PEERS\">Statistics page*</a>. For convenience, we‚Äôve included other key normalized metrics, like store listing conversions, here too. </p> <p> <strong>Track your performance with peerset comparison</strong> </p> <p> To power your decision-making and help you discover areas of opportunity, all of these new normalized metrics are launching with peerset comparison performance as standard. You‚Äôll be able to track your metrics over time and compare up to 250 different types of apps and games such as ‚ÄúMatch-3 games,‚Äù ‚ÄúAudiobooks,‚Äù or ‚ÄúComics.‚Äù </p> <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/--xDtUROQ700/YD0a4G-PzSI/AAAAAAAAQME/9y3qyQqpwLM7xuJn0I8XeCi7HEdG7lyQgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Stats%2Bpage%2Bcropped.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/--xDtUROQ700/YD0a4G-PzSI/AAAAAAAAQME/9y3qyQqpwLM7xuJn0I8XeCi7HEdG7lyQgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Stats%2Bpage%2Bcropped.png\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> <p id=\"imgCaption\"> Compare your performance to peers on the Statistics page in Google Play Console. </p> <p> Country filters allow you to customise these insights to suit your business needs. For instance, you‚Äôll be able to see if games similar to yours are driving more revenue from users in Japan, or if your team‚Äôs latest feature drop means that you‚Äôre outperforming other similar apps in terms of loyalty in India. </p> <p> During our development process, we tested this suite of new insights with select partners. As well as useful in shaping our approach, their feedback has been positive: </p> <p> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-LOLfTYfuatM/YD1dKuDVrNI/AAAAAAAAQNM/C8Sf6JDNoUgaoRW_LVqZeVfjyoVaVi7AACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-03-01%2Bat%2B4.30.11%2BPM.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: -10em; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:150px\" id=\"floatRight\" alt=\"Plarium logo\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"784\" data-original-width=\"784\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-LOLfTYfuatM/YD1dKuDVrNI/AAAAAAAAQNM/C8Sf6JDNoUgaoRW_LVqZeVfjyoVaVi7AACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-03-01%2Bat%2B4.30.11%2BPM.png\" /></a>\n     </div> <em>\"These new metrics and comparisons help drive our decision-making. Not just around what we should do with our games right now, but also strategic decisions about upcoming games. For us, it's already one of the most valuable features on the Play Console.\"</em> </p> <p> <strong>Guy Ulmer, <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/dev?id=5766366711041032164&amp;hl=en&amp;gl=US\">Plarium Global Ltd.</a> </strong> </p> <p> To help you make the most of these new metrics and insights, we‚Äôve launched a new course on <a href=\"http://g.co/playacademy/metrics\">Play Academy</a> to get you up to speed. You can also check out our <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLWz5rJ2EKKc9nK58h74i2L_jetju1Hmo8&amp;app=desktop\">masterclass webinars</a> about super-powering your growth. </p> <p> <strong>Strong privacy protections for users and developers</strong> </p> <p> The data powering these new metrics comes from users who have agreed to share their app activity with Google, and is modeled to better represent the whole population. The data simply records if an app is opened in the foreground. Users have control over their data and can opt out of sharing it, or delete individual events, in <a href=\"http://myactivity.google.com\">myactivity.google.com</a>. </p> <p> Additionally, these new developer metrics are our first to use differential privacy - an advanced technique that provides increased privacy protections across datasets. You can find out more about this approach <a href=\"https://developers.googleblog.com/2021/01/how-were-helping-developers-with-differential-privacy.html\">in our technical blog</a>. </p> <p> Just like previous benchmark launches, all of the peer comparison metrics come with protections for developer privacy. The data is generated from a large number of apps and games, and the peer groups, driven by Play Store‚Äôs advanced tagging system, do not share the performance of individual apps. So although you can find high-quality, reliable, useful peerset comparisons we've worked to obscure the performance of any individual competitor‚Äôs app from the peersets you see, and obscure your apps' performance in peersets too. </p> <p> <strong>More to come</strong> </p> <p> This is the first launch of a multi-year project to bring more helpful insights and active recommendations to Google Play Console. The largest mobile app developers often use growth consultants to help inform their long-term strategic product decisions. We‚Äôre dedicated to bringing this kind of help and expertise to <em>all</em> Play developers via the console. So look out for more launches over next year! </p> <br> <p> <small> <i>*Please note you need a Google Play Console account to access these links.</i> </small> <p> <br> \n        <center> \n
