12:52:23","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:52:23","title":"An update on Android's audio latency ","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/aDcS6zs7H00/an-update-on-androids-audio-latency.html","description":"<meta content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-SoP_7OT6zGo/YEJnBCQPS1I/AAAAAAAAQN8/pRLz9614wPQRykezF7cjncWvvpFTFFiFwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-update-on-audio-latency.png\" name=\"twitter:image\" /> \n<img src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-SoP_7OT6zGo/YEJnBCQPS1I/AAAAAAAAQN8/pRLz9614wPQRykezF7cjncWvvpFTFFiFwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-update-on-audio-latency.png\" style=\"display: none;\" /> \n<p><em>Posted by Don Turner - Android Developer Relations Engineer</em></p> \n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-SoP_7OT6zGo/YEJnBCQPS1I/AAAAAAAAQN8/pRLz9614wPQRykezF7cjncWvvpFTFFiFwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-update-on-audio-latency.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0px; text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"Header image of audio waves going through phone\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"968\" data-original-width=\"3250\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-SoP_7OT6zGo/YEJnBCQPS1I/AAAAAAAAQN8/pRLz9614wPQRykezF7cjncWvvpFTFFiFwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-update-on-audio-latency.png\" style=\"width: 100%;\" /></a>\n</div> \n<p> This article takes a look at what's changed in the Android ecosystem for audio developers recently, the audio latency of popular Android devices, and discusses Android's suitability for real-time audio apps. </p> \n<h2>What's changed?</h2> \n<p> Over the past four years we have taken a number of actions that have improved audio latency. </p> \n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-VAb0sVJS41w/YE_lpC5fwRI/AAAAAAAAQQU/ihhetZszATUCz1UuvMRDObl8Kx1T2n7_QCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/aaudio.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"timeline of key events which have had an impact on the audio latency of Android devices. Pre-2017: Google working directly with OEMs to reduce audio latency. Start 2017: AAudio - new high-performance audio API is released. Mid-2018: Oboe - an open source, C++ wrapper for AAudio and OpenSL ES is released. Mid 2019: Pixel 3A is the first 10ms Android phone. Mid 2020: OpenSL ES is deprecated. Start 2021: Oboe has 4bn+ installs\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"900\" data-original-width=\"1600\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-VAb0sVJS41w/YE_lpC5fwRI/AAAAAAAAQQU/ihhetZszATUCz1UuvMRDObl8Kx1T2n7_QCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/aaudio.png\" /></a>\n</div> \n<h2>Latency reduction</h2> \n<p> These actions, coupled with a renewed focus from device manufacturers on audio latency, have led to significant improvements in the device ecosystem. The average latency of the most popular Android phones has dropped to under 40ms, which is well within the range required for real-time applications. </p> \n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-VqGMk9xtzW4/YDboJ5iDsZI/AAAAAAAAQJQ/3DU5kl_c-awndCSzUwF59PDgxsMrcGmMQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B3.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0px; text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"bar graph showing average audio latency of 20 most popular Android phones. In Jan 2017 it was 109 milliseconds. In Jan 2021 it was 39 milliseconds.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"946\" data-original-width=\"1290\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-VqGMk9xtzW4/YDboJ5iDsZI/AAAAAAAAQJQ/3DU5kl_c-awndCSzUwF59PDgxsMrcGmMQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B3.png\" style=\"width: 100%;\" /></a>\n</div>\n<p id=\"imgCaption\">device popularity source: <a href=\"https://www.appbrain.com/stats/top-android-phones\">appbrain.com</a></p> \n<h2>Greater consistency</h2> \n<p>Digging into the data we can see that in 2017 there was a significant difference between the highest and lowest values (222ms).</p> \n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Ic_vdBVC5HM/YDbpBT2nnAI/AAAAAAAAQJY/aPJLmTFxUX8BDA5OaiZ1MHE6YDilcP-uQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B4.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0px; text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"bar graph showing audio latency of most popular Android phones in Jan 2017. There are 19 in total, all of which are Samsung Galaxy models. The average latency is 109ms, smallest value is 36ms, highest is 258ms, range is 222ms.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"694\" data-original-width=\"1240\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Ic_vdBVC5HM/YDbpBT2nnAI/AAAAAAAAQJY/aPJLmTFxUX8BDA5OaiZ1MHE6YDilcP-uQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B4.png\" style=\"width: 100%;\" /></a>\n</div>\n<p id=\"imgCaption\">device popularity source: <a href=\"https://www.appbrain.com/stats/top-android-phones\">appbrain.com</a></p> \n<p> Compare that to the data for 2021. The range has reduced by a factor of 8 to just 28ms, providing a far more consistent audio experience. This is more impressive when you consider that there are now multiple OEMs on the most-popular list, compared to only a single manufacturer in 2017. In addition, many of the devices on the list are not high-end flagship models. </p> \n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ZycUtpkWu8I/YDbpmeIYajI/AAAAAAAAQJg/FMR0U_HG6x0jd1tFggfZDVZ2jmQw_d1wACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B5.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0px; text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"bar graph showing audio latency of most popular Android phones in Jan 2021. There are 20 in total, with models from Samsung, Redmi, Oppo, Huawei and Vivo. The average latency is 39ms, smallest value is 28ms, highest is 56ms, range is 28ms.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"674\" data-original-width=\"1180\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ZycUtpkWu8I/YDbpmeIYajI/AAAAAAAAQJg/FMR0U_HG6x0jd1tFggfZDVZ2jmQw_d1wACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image%2B5.png\" style=\"width: 100%;\" /></a>\n</div>\n<p id=\"imgCaption\">device popularity source: <a href=\"https://www.appbrain.com/stats/top-android-phones\">appbrain.com</a></p> \n<h2>Tap-to-tone latency</h2> \n<p> Up to now I've been referring to round-trip audio latency. Round-trip latency involves three components in the audio chain: audio input, audio processing and audio output. </p> \n<p> Many real-time audio apps generate audio from screen tap events rather than relying on input audio. These kinds of apps are sensitive to \"tap-to-tone\" latency - the time taken from tapping on the screen to hearing a sound. The latency introduced by tapping <a href=\"https://github.com/google/walt/blob/master/docs/TapLatency.md\">the touch screen is anywhere from 10-35ms</a>, with 20ms being fairly typical on modern Android devices. </p> \n<p> To estimate tap-to-tone latency given round-trip latency, you can subtract the audio input latency (typically 5ms), and add the touch latency (typically 20ms). In other words, add 15ms to the round-trip latency. Given the numbers above, this means the average tap-to-tone latency of the most popular android phones is also well under that required for most real-time audio applications. </p> \n<h2>Looking to the future</h2> \n<p> Despite the significant reductions in audio latency across the Android ecosystem our work is nowhere near complete. 20ms round-tip latency is required for<a href=\"https://source.android.com/compatibility/11/android-11-cdd#5_10_professional_audio\"> Android professional audio apps</a>, and 10ms remains the long term goal. And at this time some less popular devices still have high audio latency. However, if you have been holding back on developing an Android app because of audio latency, it might be time to reconsider. </p> \n<p> To get started, check out the <a href=\"https://github.com/google/oboe/blob/master/docs/GettingStarted.md\">Oboe getting started guide</a> or <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=csfHAbr5ilI&amp;list=PLWz5rJ2EKKc_duWv9IPNvx9YBudNMmLSa\">video tutorials</a>. </p> \n<h2>Data sources and tools</h2> \n<p> <a href=\"https://github.com/google/oboe/tree/master/apps/OboeTester/docs\">OboeTester</a> </p> \n<p> <a href=\"https://github.com/google/walt\">WALT</a> </p> \n<p> <a src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-6fNVuYUzbmE/YDRI8cdnkmI/AAAAAAAAQH0/2U_XEL2r4LMYeWJbRHnVHrhaA-FrjEKywCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/JCM21013_Thumbnails-03.jpg\"> <p><em>Posted by The Jetpack Compose Team </em><p> <p> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose\">Jetpack Compose</a> is Android‚Äôs modern toolkit for building native UI. It enables you to quickly bring your app to life with less code, powerful tools, and intuitive Kotlin APIs. With the <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/02/announcing-jetpack-compose-beta.html\">Beta of Jetpack Compose</a> released today, this is the perfect time to learn Compose and get ready to adopt it. To help you get started with Jetpack Compose we are launching a new #AndroidDevChallenge! </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/sZK3HSX4cRU\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <p> For the next four weeks, the #AndroidDevChallenge will be launching a series of weekly challenges to help you build better apps faster with Jetpack Compose. Oriented around ‚Äúlift off insights,\" each challenge focuses on a new area of Compose, from animations to Material Theming, composables to lists and more! Compete to win new prizes for each challenge, with over one thousand prizes to win including a Pixel 5.<small> <sup>1</sup> </small> The first challenge starts today! </p> <h2>The challenges</h2> <p> Every week brings a new challenge with its own rules and tasks. Every Wednesday starting today we‚Äôll publish a blog post containing the full description of what you need to do and how long you have to complete the task. Each challenge will help you get familiar with the compose <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/mental-model\">mental model</a> and different Compose APIs - from basic Composables like <code> Text </code> and <code> List,</code> to state, animations and more. </p> <p> Your solution to each challenge must be implemented in a GitHub repository. Make a copy of this <a href=\"http://goo.gle/adc-template\">Github repository template</a> and follow the instructions in the README. The template contains a basic <code>Hello World!</code> in Compose and a continuous integration setup. </p> <h2>Week #1 - Puppy adoption app</h2> \n    <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-d6KGTLsbI3M/YDQSlsM1LXI/AAAAAAAAQHQ/bFFOakT2je4o-y0oPCfW9gzBjuqmfi4dQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-02-11%2Bat%2B10.58.49.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: -10em; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:200px\" id=\"floatLeft\" alt=\"Android 12 logo\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"784\" data-original-width=\"784\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-d6KGTLsbI3M/YDQSlsM1LXI/AAAAAAAAQHQ/bFFOakT2je4o-y0oPCfW9gzBjuqmfi4dQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-02-11%2Bat%2B10.58.49.png\" /></a>\n    </div> <p> Let‚Äôs start the #AndroidDevChallenge with a <del>bang</del> bark: build a puppy adoption app! The app should contain an overview screen that displays <strong>a list of puppies</strong>, and a <strong>detail screen</strong> showing each puppy's details. You have until <strong>March 2nd, 23:59 PST to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/dev-challenge#the-latest-challenge\">submit your entry. </a> </strong> <small> <sup>2</sup> </small> </p> <p> Your UI must be fully built in Compose. Your submission will only be judged based on your app‚Äôs UI layer. To help you with the implementation, check out the Compose documentation on <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/layout\">layouts</a>, <a href=\"https://youtu.be/BhqPpUYJYeQ\">lists</a>, text and navigation. For some paws-on learning try out the <a href=\"https://goo.gle/compose-pathway\">Compose pathway</a>, with codelabs covering several topics useful in completing this challenge. </p> <p> Are you a üê±rather than a üê∂ person? Submissions for any type of pet adoption app are welcomed. </p> <p> We look forward to seeing what you build! </p> <h2>This week‚Äôs prize</h2> <p> Our first challenge kicks off with a prize that makes for the perfect sidekick as you‚Äôre flying through Compose: a limited edition trophy of our Jetpack Compose superhero, made of LEGO bricks. The first 500 people to successfully complete this challenge and submit their entry can add this trophy to their collection of Android figurines, showing off how you‚Äôre a winner for the first week‚Äôs #AndroidDevChallenge. </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1PGx_uf4kVs/YDRRg0JlwSI/AAAAAAAAQIA/PBpnzWNqsashjrqb05oO0MBWRuBbw0YegCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Lego%2BTrophy%2BAnimation_Overlay.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img id=\"imgFull\" style=\"width:100%\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1PGx_uf4kVs/YDRRg0JlwSI/AAAAAAAAQIA/PBpnzWNqsashjrqb05oO0MBWRuBbw0YegCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Lego%2BTrophy%2BAnimation_Overlay.gif\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <p id=\"imgCaption\">Week #1 prize: Jetpack Compose superhero</p> <h2>Help make Jetpack Compose better</h2> <p> Community is at the heart of Jetpack Compose and your feedback helps us build a better product: </p> \n    <ul> \n     <li>File issues with Jetpack Compose on the official <a href=\"http://goo.gle/compose-feedback\">issue tracker</a>. <li><a href=\"https://g.co/userresearch/androiddev21\">Sign up</a> to be part of the Jetpack Compose research studies. </li> </li>\n    </ul> <br> <br> <small> <sup>1</sup> There will be new prizes for each week‚Äôs challenge; for weeks when a Google Pixel 5 is a prize, we will offer a similarly valued electronics gift card for winners that reside in a country where a Google Pixel 5 is unavailable. 12:52:23","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:52:23","title":"Android 12 Developer Preview 2","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/ODwhBM8xdhM/android-12-developer-preview-2.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/--LuXJTDz_vI/YFIgU1spOkI/AAAAAAAAQRI/Cku9StJJwVoDiWXZkfg0i2H-aSYaogeDgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android%2B12_logo.png\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/--LuXJTDz_vI/YFIgU1spOkI/AAAAAAAAQRI/Cku9StJJwVoDiWXZkfg0i2H-aSYaogeDgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android%2B12_logo.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Dave Burke, VP of Engineering </em><p> \n    <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2WiKDQwO6nI/YC2vlLLtUyI/AAAAAAAAQFM/lje72qqUt74m22FTZZx_0VmfFnfjODSiACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image6.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: -10em; text-align: center; \"><img id=\"floatRight\" alt=\"Android 12 logo\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"784\" data-original-width=\"784\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2WiKDQwO6nI/YC2vlLLtUyI/AAAAAAAAQFM/lje72qqUt74m22FTZZx_0VmfFnfjODSiACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image6.png\" /></a>\n    </div> <p> Last month we shared the <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/02/android-12-dp1.html\">first preview of Android 12</a>, an early look at the next version of Android. Today we‚Äôre bringing you the next milestone build in this year‚Äôs release, with more new features and changes for you to try with your apps. Our program of early previews is driven by our core philosophy of openness and collaboration with you, our community. Your input helps us make Android a better platform for developers and users, so keep the feedback coming! </p> <p> In Android 12 we‚Äôre making the OS smarter, easier to use, and better performing, with privacy and security at the core. We‚Äôre also working to give you new tools for building great experiences for users, whether they‚Äôre using phones, laptops, tablets, TVs, or cars. Some things to look for in today‚Äôs release include new rounded corners APIs, improved picture-in-picture APIs, better companion device management, easier effects like blur and color filter, app overlay controls, and more. </p> <p> There‚Äôs a lot to check out in Developer Preview 2 - read on for a few highlights and <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12\">visit the Android 12 developer site</a> for details and downloads for Pixel. For those already running Developer Preview 1 or 1.1, we‚Äôre also offering an over-the-air (OTA) update to today‚Äôs release. </p> <p> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/feedback\">Let us know what you think</a>, and thank you to everyone who has shared such great feedback so far. </p> \n    <section> \n     <h2><strong>Trust and safety</strong></h2> \n     <p> We‚Äôre continuing to focus on giving users more transparency and control while keeping their devices and data secure. In today‚Äôs release, we‚Äôve added some new features to check out and test with your apps. </p> \n     <p> <strong>App overlay controls</strong> - Android‚Äôs system alert window gives apps a way to get users‚Äô attention for important actions by showing an overlay on top of the active app. These windows can interrupt the user, though, so we already require apps to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/Manifest.permission#SYSTEM_ALERT_WINDOW\">request permission</a> before displaying them. Now in Android 12 we‚Äôre giving you control over whether these overlays can be shown over your content. After you‚Äôve declared <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/Manifest.permission#HIDE_OVERLAY_WINDOWS\">a new permission</a>, your app can call <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/Window#setHideOverlayWindows(boolean)\">Window#setHideOverlayWindows()</a> to indicate that all <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/WindowManager.LayoutParams#TYPE_APPLICATION_OVERLAY\">TYPE_APPLICATION_OVERLAY</a> windows should be hidden when your app‚Äôs window is visible. You might choose to do this when displaying sensitive screens, such as transaction confirmation flows. More <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features#hide-application-overlay-windows\">here</a>. </p> \n    </section> \n    <section> \n     <p> <strong>Extended security for lockscreen notification actions</strong> - Android 12 adds finer-grained privacy and security controls for notifications displayed on the device lockscreen. You can now <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/Notification.Action.Builder#setAuthenticationRequired(boolean)\">configure notification actions</a> so that when triggered from the lockscreen, they will always generate an authentication challenge. This extends the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/Notification#visibility\">notification visibility</a> controls already available through the notification APIs. For example, this enables a messaging app to require authentication before deleting a message or marking it as read. More <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features#notification-secure\">here</a>. </p> \n    </section> \n    <section> \n     <p> \n      <div class=\"container\" id=\"app-digest\"></div> <strong>Access to app digests </strong> - For apps that need to validate the integrity of app packages installed on Android devices, we‚Äôre introducing a new API that lets you query the platform directly for the checksum of an installed app. You can choose from several digest algorithms such as SHA256, SHA512, Merkle Root, and others. To request a checksum, call <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/content/pm/PackageManager#requestChecksums(java.lang.String,%20boolean,%20int,%20java.util.List%3Cjava.security.cert.Certificate%3E,%20android.content.pm.PackageManager.OnChecksumsReadyListener)\">PackageManager.requestChecksums()</a> with an app‚Äôs package name, the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/content/pm/Checksum\">checksum types</a> you need, the installer certs you trust, and a listener to receive the checksums. The platform returns the matching checksums, either precomputed and provided by the installer app (such as Google Play) or computed by the platform. Results are filtered based on <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/basics/intents/package-visibility\">package visibility</a> guidelines, so you‚Äôll need to declare the packages of interest in your manifest. This new API provides a simpler, more efficient way to obtain checksums and gives you the stability of a standard, public API that‚Äôs optimized for speed and security. For backward compatibility, we‚Äôre working on a Jetpack library that provides the same functionality back to API 15 - watch for more details coming soon. </p> \n    </section> <p> You can read more about these and other privacy and security changes <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-12\">here</a>. </p> \n    <section> \n     <h2><strong>Better user experience tools</strong></h2> \n     <p> We‚Äôre working to give you more tools to help you deliver a polished experience and better performance for users. Here are some of the updates in today‚Äôs release. </p> \n    </section> \n    <section> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-lQIPkRs7ZgI/YFIYdcMx59I/AAAAAAAAQQw/iSqQbAyUByQDFHXpJH22H5oDs0TZXLAeACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/rounded_abs.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: -10em; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:180px\" id=\"floatRight\" alt=\"rounded corners\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"784\" data-original-width=\"784\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-lQIPkRs7ZgI/YFIYdcMx59I/AAAAAAAAQQw/iSqQbAyUByQDFHXpJH22H5oDs0TZXLAeACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/rounded_abs.png\" /></a>\n     </div> \n     <p> <strong>Support for Rounded corners</strong> - Many modern devices use screens with rounded corners, giving them a clean modern look, but also introducing some extra considerations for app developers. To deliver a great UX on these devices, developers need to account for the rounded corners and adjust any nearby UI elements to prevent them from being truncated. </p> \n     <p> To help with this, we‚Äôre introducing new APIs to let you query for rounded corners and get their details. A <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/RoundedCorner?hl=en\">RoundedCorner</a> holds the details for a corner, including its radius, centerpoint, and other data. You can call <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/Display#getRoundedCorner(int)\">Display.getRoundedCorner()</a> to get the absolute details for each rounded corner. You can also call <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/WindowInsets#getRoundedCorner(int)\">WindowInsets.getRoundedCorner(</a>) to get the corner details relative to your app‚Äôs bounds. With these, you can manage the position of UI elements and content as needed. More <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features#rounded_corner_apis\">here</a>. </p> \n    </section> \n    <section> \n     <p> <strong>Picture in Picture (PIP) improvements</strong> - for people using gesture nav, we‚Äôve improved how apps transition to picture-in-picture (PIP) mode on swipe up-to-home. If an app enables <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/PictureInPictureParams.Builder#setAutoEnterEnabled(boolean)\">auto-PIP</a>, the system now directly transitions the app to PIP mode on up-to-home, instead of waiting for the up-to-home animation to complete. This makes the transition smoother and improves perceived performance. We‚Äôve also improved PIP window resizing for non-video content. Apps can now <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/PictureInPictureParams.Builder#setSeamlessResizeEnabled(boolean)\">enable seamless resize</a> to let the system resize the PIP Activity when needed. Android 12 also supports stashing the PiP window by dragging it to the left or right edge of the screen. Also, to make PIP windows easier to manipulate, we‚Äôve updated the tap behaviors. Single-tapping now displays controls, and double-tapping toggles the PIP window size. More <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features/pip-improvements\">here</a>. </p> \n    </section> \n    <section> \n     <p> <strong>Keeping companion device apps awake </strong>- For apps that manage companion devices like smartwatches and fitness trackers, it can be a challenge to make sure the app is running and connected whenever an associated companion device is nearby. To make this easier, we‚Äôre extending the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/companion/CompanionDeviceManager\">Companion Device Manager</a> with a new <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/companion/CompanionDeviceService\">CompanionDeviceService API</a>. Apps that manage companion devices can implement this service to let the system wake the app whenever the associated companion device is nearby. The system keeps the service bound whenever the device is nearby, and notifies the service when the device goes in and out of range or is turned off, to let the app clean up state as needed. Apps can also use a new <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/companion/AssociationRequest.Builder#setDeviceProfile(java.lang.String)\">companion device profile</a> when connecting to a watch, which simplifies enrollment by bundling related permissions into a single grant. More <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features#keep-awake\">here</a>. </p> \n    </section> \n    <section> \n     <p> <strong>Bandwidth estimation improvements</strong> - for developers who need to know the typical bandwidth available to each user so you can tailor their experience, we now provide improved bandwidth estimation. We‚Äôve enhanced the existing <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/11/features/5g#estimator\">bandwidth estimation APIs</a> to let you retrieve an estimate of aggregate throughput per carrier or Wi-Fi SSID, network type, and signal level, for all users on the device. The new estimation is likely to be easier and more accurate than most other estimation methods, give it a try and let us know how it works for you. </p> \n     <section> \n      <p> <strong>Easier blurs, color filters and other effects </strong>- In Android 12, we‚Äôre making it easier to apply common graphics effects to your Views and rendering hierarchies. You can use <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/RenderEffect\">RenderEffect</a> to apply blurs, color filters, and more to any <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/RenderNode\">RenderNode</a>. You can combine these effects as chain effects (which compose an inner and outer effect in order) or blend them. You can also apply effects directly to Views (leveraging the underlying RenderNode) by calling <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View#setRenderEffect(android.graphics.RenderEffect)\">View.setRenderEffect(RenderEffect)</a>. </p> \n      <pre class=\"prettyprint\">\nview.setRenderEffect(RenderEffect.createBlurEffect(radiusX, radiusY, SHADER_TILE_MODE))\n</pre> \n      <center> \n       <p id=\"imgCaption\"> Blurring a View with RenderEffect </p>\n      </center> \n      <p> This allows you to blur the contents of an <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/widget/ImageView\">ImageView</a> without having to get the bitmap data, process the image, create a new <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/Bitmap\">Bitmap</a>, and set it back into the ImageView. RenderEffect leverages the existing rendering pipeline to minimize excess calculation. </p> \n      <p> Give these a try and let use know what you think! More <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features#rendereffect\">here</a>. </p> \n      <p> You can also create a frosted glass effect for your window background using a new <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/Window#setBackgroundBlurRadius(int)\">Window.setBackgroundBlurRadius()</a> API. With this you can set a radius to control the density and scope and the platform applies the blur to the background content within the bounds of your app‚Äôs window only. You can also use <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/WindowManager.LayoutParams#blurBehindRadius\">blurBehindRadius</a> to blur all of the content behind the window to create a depth effect for a floating window. </p> \n      <center> \n       <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-H8KalWgHCGE/YFIbLJYlxpI/AAAAAAAAQQ4/IfPpjm68v3sxN56M9KMZZfgZxRfEMNJmgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/demo-dialog-dp2-blogpost-3.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:300px\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-H8KalWgHCGE/YFIbLJYlxpI/AAAAAAAAQQ4/IfPpjm68v3sxN56M9KMZZfgZxRfEMNJmgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/demo-dialog-dp2-blogpost-3.png\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n       <p id=\"imgCaption\">A dialog window with background blur and blur behind... </p>\n      </center> \n     </section> \n     <section> \n      <h2><strong>App compatibility</strong></h2> \n      <p> We‚Äôre working to make updates faster and smoother by prioritizing app compatibility as we roll out new platform versions. In Android 12, we‚Äôve made most app-facing changes opt-in to give you more time, and we‚Äôve updated our tools and processes to help you get ready sooner. </p> \n      <p> With Developer Preview 2, we‚Äôre well into the release and continuing to improve overall stability, so now is the time to try the new features and changes and give us your feedback. We‚Äôre especially looking for input on our APIs, as well as details on how the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-all\">platform changes</a> affect your apps. Please visit the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/feedback\">feedback page</a> to share your thoughts with us or report issues. </p> \n      <center> \n       <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-U4hDHhnmehE/YFI1uP1kv0I/AAAAAAAAQRQ/hHjFVBxNDh8OOkOfq34AN-a_hZPxAmHLwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/android-12-desktop-timeline-en-overpg%2B%25281%2529.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-U4hDHhnmehE/YFI1uP1kv0I/AAAAAAAAQRQ/hHjFVBxNDh8OOkOfq34AN-a_hZPxAmHLwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/android-12-desktop-timeline-en-overpg%2B%25281%2529.png\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n      </center> \n      <p> It‚Äôs also a good time to start your <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/migration\">compatibility testing</a> and identify any work you‚Äôll need to do. We recommend doing the work early, so you can release a compatible update by Android 12 Beta 1. There‚Äôs no need to change your app‚Äôs targetSdkVersion at this time, but we do recommend using the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/reference/compat-framework-changes\">behavior change toggles</a> to get a preliminary idea of how your app might be affected by opt-in changes in Android 12. </p> \n      <p> As we reach <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/overview#platform_stability\">Platform Stability</a> in August 2021, all of the app-facing system behaviors, SDK/NDK APIs, and non-SDK lists will be finalized. At that point, you can wind up your final compatibility testing and release a fully compatible version of your app, SDK, or library. More on the timeline for developers is <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/preview/overview\">here</a>. </p> \n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Q18mvR8f2DY/YFIe-fl83EI/AAAAAAAAQRE/ssOMv8fyR6oU3sD5MchxNrZxOfq1XSxRwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/compat_toggles_crop.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:300px\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Q18mvR8f2DY/YFIe-fl83EI/AAAAAAAAQRE/ssOMv8fyR6oU3sD5MchxNrZxOfq1XSxRwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/compat_toggles_crop.png\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n      <p id=\"imgCaption\"> App compatibility toggles in Developer Options. </p> \n     </section> \n     <section> \n      <h1>Get started with Android 12</h1> \n      <p> The Developer Preview has everything you need to try the Android 12 features, test your apps, and give us <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/feedback\">feedback</a>. You can get started today by <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/download\">flashing a device system image</a> to a <strong>Pixel 3 / 3 XL</strong>, <strong>Pixel 3a / 3a XL</strong>, <strong>Pixel 4 / 4 XL</strong>, <strong>Pixel 4a / 4a 5G</strong>, or <strong>Pixel 5</strong> device or using the Android Emulator. If you‚Äôve already installed a preview build to your Pixel device, you‚Äôll automatically get future updates over-the-air for all later previews and Betas. 12:52:23","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:52:23","title":"First preview of Android 12","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/W5Dy7eBfh0Q/android-12-dp1.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-eRnBIDn-ZZE/YC6eGA2hC5I/AAAAAAAAQGY/bea6RxVXWcs9q5FoLEZtjuTnLZvegzY2ACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android%2B12_logo.png\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-eRnBIDn-ZZE/YC6eGA2hC5I/AAAAAAAAQGY/bea6RxVXWcs9q5FoLEZtjuTnLZvegzY2ACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android%2B12_logo.png\"> \n  <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n   <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2WiKDQwO6nI/YC2vlLLtUyI/AAAAAAAAQFM/lje72qqUt74m22FTZZx_0VmfFnfjODSiACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image6.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: -10em; text-align: center; \"><img <p> Every day, Android apps help billions of people work, play, communicate, and create on a wide range of devices from phones and laptops to tablets, TVs, and cars. As more people come to rely on the experiences you build, their expectations can rise just as fast. It‚Äôs one of the reasons we share Android releases with you early: your feedback helps us build a better platform for your apps and all of the people who use them. Today, we‚Äôre releasing the first Developer Preview of Android 12, the next version of Android, for your testing and feedback. </p> <p> With each version, we‚Äôre working to make the OS smarter, easier to use, and better performing, with privacy and security at the core. In Android 12 we‚Äôre also working to give you new tools for building great experiences for users. Starting with things like compatible media transcoding, which helps your app to work with the latest video formats if you don‚Äôt already support them, and easier copy/paste of rich content into your apps, like images and videos. We‚Äôre also adding privacy protections and optimizing performance to keep your apps responsive. </p> <p> Today‚Äôs first preview is just the start for Android 12, and we‚Äôll have lots more to share as we move through the release. Read on for a taste of what‚Äôs new in Android 12, and visit the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12\">Android 12 developer site</a> for details on <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/download\">downloads for Pixel</a> and release <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/overview#timeline\">timeline</a>. As always, it‚Äôs crucial to get your feedback early, to help us incorporate it into the final product, so <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/feedback\">let us know what you think</a>! </p> <p> Alongside the work we‚Äôre doing in Android 12, later this month we‚Äôll have more to share on another important tool that helps you create great user experiences more easily: Jetpack Compose, our modern toolkit for building native UI. <a href=\"http://goo.gle/TheAndroidShow\">Join us on #TheAndroidShow</a> for a behind-the-scenes look at Jetpack Compose, livestreamed on February 24 at 9AM PT, and tweet your Jetpack Compose questions using #TheAndroidShow to have them answered live on the show. </p> <h2><strong>Trust and safety</strong></h2> <p> Privacy is at the heart of everything we do, and in Android 12 we‚Äôre continuing to focus on giving users more transparency and control while keeping their devices and data secure. In today‚Äôs release we‚Äôve added new controls over identifiers that can be used for tracking, safer defaults for app components, and more. These changes may affect your apps, so we recommend testing as soon as possible. Watch for more privacy and security features coming in later preview releases. </p> <p> <strong>Modern SameSite cookie behaviors in WebView</strong> - In line with <a href=\"https://blog.chromium.org/2020/02/samesite-cookie-changes-in-february.html\">changes to Chrome</a> and other browsers, WebView includes new SameSite cookie behaviors to provide additional security and privacy and give users more transparency and control over how cookies can be used across sites. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-12#samesite\">More here</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Restricted Netlink MAC </strong>- We‚Äôre continuing to help developers migrate to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/articles/user-data-ids\">privacy-protecting resettable identifiers</a>. In a multi-release effort to ease migration of device-scoped Netlink MAC, in Android 11 we restricted access to it based on API level 30, and in Android 12 we‚Äôre applying the restriction for all apps - regardless of targetSDK level. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-all#mac-address\">More here</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Safer exporting of components - </strong>To prevent apps from inadvertently exporting activities, services, and receivers, we‚Äôre changing the default handling of the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/activity-element#exported\">android:exported</a> attribute to be more explicit. With this change, components that declare one or more intent filters must now explicitly declare an android:exported attribute. You should inspect your components in the manifest in order to avoid installation errors related to this change. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-12#exported\">More here</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Safer handling of Intents</strong> - To make handling PendingIntents more secure, Android 12 requires apps to explicitly declare a mutability flag, either <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/PendingIntent#FLAG_MUTABLE\">FLAG_MUTABLE</a> or the new <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/PendingIntent#FLAG_IMMUTABLE\">FLAG_IMMUTABLE</a>, for each PendingIntent. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-12#pending-intent-mutability\">More here</a>. </p> <p> You can read more about these and other privacy and security changes <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-12\">here</a>. </p> <h2><strong>Better user experience tools</strong></h2> <p> In Android 12 we‚Äôre investing in key areas to help deliver a polished experience and better performance for users. Here are some of the updates so far. </p> <p> <strong>Compatible media transcoding</strong> - With the prevalence of HEVC hardware encoders on mobile devices, camera apps are increasingly capturing in HEVC format, which offers significant improvements in quality and compression over older codecs. Most apps should support HEVC, but for apps that can‚Äôt, we‚Äôre introducing compatible media transcoding. </p> <p> With this feature, an app that doesn‚Äôt support HEVC can have the platform automatically transcode the file into AVC, a format that is widely compatible. The transcoding process takes time, depending on the video and hardware properties of the device. As an example, a one minute 1080p video at 30fps takes around 9 seconds to transcode on a Pixel 4. You can opt-in to use the transcoding service by just declaring the media formats that your apps don't support. For developers, we strongly recommend that your apps support HEVC, and if that‚Äôs not possible, enable compatible media transcoding. The feature will be active on all devices using HEVC format for video capture. We'd love to hear your feedback on this feature. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features/compatible-media-transcoding\">More here</a>. </p> <p> <strong>AVIF image support</strong> - To give you higher image quality with more efficient compression, Android 12 introduces platform support for <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AV1#AV1_Image_File_Format_(AVIF)\">AV1 Image File Format</a> (AVIF). AVIF is a container format for images and sequences of images encoded using <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AV1\">AV1</a>. Like other modern image formats, AVIF takes advantage of the intra-frame encoded content from video compression. This dramatically improves image quality for the same file size when compared to older image formats, such as JPEG. </p> <p id=\"floatLeft\"> AVIF (18.2kB) </p> <p id=\"floatRight\"> JPEG (20.7kB) </p> \n    <div id=\"flexParent\"> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-bj8bL6ZacSs/YC2xpy2BjAI/AAAAAAAAQFY/lCoN7T0pPYQRiSG-KRZR9B5FgBMtOCnfACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image4.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img id=\"flexImg\" alt=\"race car photo in AVIF (18.2kB)\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1080\" data-original-width=\"1920\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-bj8bL6ZacSs/YC2xpy2BjAI/AAAAAAAAQFY/lCoN7T0pPYQRiSG-KRZR9B5FgBMtOCnfACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image4.png\" /></a>\n     </div> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ZuSZwuWeEd8/YC2x41ZKVFI/AAAAAAAAQFc/fKV3tQUcTn47sInNKfJsEMddbUOsZogYACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image2.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img id=\"flexImg\" alt=\"race car photo in JPEG (20.7kB)\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1080\" data-original-width=\"1920\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ZuSZwuWeEd8/YC2x41ZKVFI/AAAAAAAAQFc/fKV3tQUcTn47sInNKfJsEMddbUOsZogYACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image2.png\" /></a>\n     </div> \n    </div> <p id=\"imgCaption\"> Credit: <a href=\"https://jakearchibald.com/2020/avif-has-landed/demos/compare/?show=f1&amp;img=/c/f1-match-ff75e344.jpg\">Image comparison</a> from <a href=\"https://jakearchibald.com/2020/avif-has-landed/\">AVIF has landed</a> by Jake Archibald </p> <p> <strong>Foreground service optimizations</strong> - Foreground services are an important way for apps to manage certain types of user-facing tasks, but when overused they can affect performance and even lead to app kills. To ensure a better experience for users, we will be blocking foreground service starts from the background for apps that are targeting the new platform. To make it easier to transition away from this pattern, we‚Äôre introducing a new <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/job/JobParameters.html#isExpeditedJob()\">expedited job</a> in JobScheduler that gets elevated process priority, network access, and runs immediately regardless of power constraints like Battery Saver or Doze. For back-compatibility, we‚Äôve also built expedited jobs into the latest release of <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/topic/libraries/architecture/workmanager\">Jetpack WorkManager library</a>. Also, to reduce distraction for users, we‚Äôre now delaying the display of some foreground service notifications by up to 10 seconds. This gives short-lived tasks a chance to complete before their notifications are shown. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-12#foreground-service-launch-restrictions\">More here</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Rich content insertion </strong>- Users love images, videos and other expressive content, but inserting and moving this content in apps is not always easy. To make it simple for your apps to receive rich content, we‚Äôre introducing a new unified API that lets you accept content from any source: clipboard, keyboard, or drag and drop. You can attach a new interface, <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/OnReceiveContentListener\">OnReceiveContentListener</a>, to UI components and get a callback when content is inserted through any mechanism. This callback becomes the single place for your code to handle insertion of all content, from plain and styled text to markup, images, videos, audio files, and more. For back-compatibility, we‚Äôve added the unified API to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/androidx/core/view/OnReceiveContentListener\">AndroidX</a>. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features/unified-content-api\">More here</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Audio-coupled haptic effect</strong> - In Android 12 apps can provide audio-coupled haptic feedback through the phone's vibrator. The vibration strength and frequency are derived from an audio session, allowing you to create more immersive game and audio experiences. For example, a video calling app could use custom ringtones to identify the caller through haptic feedback, or you could simulate rough terrain in a racing game. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/media/audiofx/HapticGenerator\">More here</a>. </p> \n    <!--\n<p>\n<strong>Multi-channel audio</strong> - Android 12 includes several enhancements for audio with spatial information. It adds support for MPEG-H playback in passthrough and offload mode, and the audio mixers, resamplers and effects have been optimized for up to 24 channels (the previous maximum was 8). \n</p>\n<p> --> <strong>Immersive mode API improvements for gesture nav </strong>- We‚Äôve simplified immersive mode so that gesture navigation is easier and more consistent, for example when watching a video, reading a book, or playing a game. We‚Äôre still <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/WindowInsetsController#BEHAVIOR_SHOW_TRANSIENT_BARS_BY_SWIPE\">protecting apps from accidental gestures</a> when in full-screen experiences related to gaming, but in all other full-screen or immersive experiences (e.g. video viewers, reading, photo gallery), for apps targeting the new platform, we‚Äôre changing the default to allow users to navigate their phone with one swipe. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-12#immersive-mode-improvements\">More here</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Notification UI updates </strong>- We‚Äôre refreshing notification designs to make them more modern, easier to use, and more functional. In this first preview you‚Äôll notice changes from the drawer and controls to the templates themselves. We‚Äôre also optimizing transitions and animations across the system to make them more smooth. As part of the updates, for apps targeting Android 12 we‚Äôre decorating notifications with custom content with icon and expand affordances to match all other notifications. <a href=\"http://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-12#custom-notifications\">More here</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Faster, more responsive notifications</strong> - When users tap a notification, they expect to jump immediately into the app - the faster the better. To meet that expectation, developers should make sure that notification taps trigger Activity starts directly, rather than using ‚Äútrampolines‚Äù - an intermediary broadcast receiver or service - to start the Activity. Notification trampolines can cause significant delays and affect the user experience. To keep notifications responsive, Android 12 will block notification trampolines by preventing them from launching their target Activities, and we‚Äôre asking developers to migrate away from this pattern. The change applies only to apps targeting the new platform, but for all apps we‚Äôll display a toast to make trampolines visible to you and to users. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-12#notification-trampolines\">More here</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Improved Binder IPC calls </strong> - As part of our work on performance, we‚Äôve put a focus on reducing system variability. We‚Äôve taken a look at latency and workload distribution, and made optimizations that reduce the median experience from the tail end, or 99% percentile use case. In doing so, we‚Äôve targeted improvements to system binder calls adding lightweight caching strategies and focusing on removing lock contention to improve latency distribution. This has yielded roughly a 2x performance increase on Binder calls overall, with significant improvements in specific calls, for example a 47x improvement in <code>refContentProvider()</code>, 15x in <code>releaseWakeLock()</code>, and 7.9x in <code>JobScheduler.schedule()</code>. </p> <h2><strong>App compatibility</strong></h2> <p> We‚Äôre working to make updates faster and smoother by prioritizing app compatibility as we roll out new platform versions. In Android 12 we‚Äôve made most app-facing changes opt-in to give you more time, and we‚Äôve updated our tools and processes to help you get ready sooner. We‚Äôve also added new functionality to Google Play system updates to give your apps a better environment on Android 12 devices. </p> <p> <strong>More of Android updated through Google Play </strong>- We‚Äôre continuing to expand our investment in <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2019/05/fresher-os-with-projects-treble-and-mainline.html\">Google Play system updates</a> (Project Mainline) to give apps a more consistent, secure environment across devices. In Android 12 we‚Äôve added the Android Runtime (ART) module that lets us push updates to the core runtime and libraries on devices running Android 12. We can improve runtime performance and correctness, manage memory more efficiently, and make Kotlin operations faster - all without requiring a full system update. We‚Äôve also expanded the functionality of existing modules - for example, we‚Äôre delivering our compatible media transcoding feature inside an updatable module. </p> <p> <strong>Optimizing for tablets, foldables, and TVs </strong>- With more people than ever using apps on large-screen devices like foldables, tablets, and TVs, now is a great time to make sure your app or game is ready. Get started by <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/docs/quality-guidelines/tablet-app-quality\">optimizing for tablets</a> and <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/ui/foldables\">building apps for foldables</a>. And, for the biggest screen in the home, the first Android 12 preview for Android TV is also available. In addition to bringing the latest Android features to the TV with this preview, you will also be able to test your apps on the all-new Google TV experience. Learn more on the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/tv\">Android TV Developers</a> site and get started with your <a href=\"https://store.askey.com/adt-3.html\">ADT-3 developer kit</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Updated lists of non-SDK interfaces</strong> - We‚Äôve restricted additional <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/non-sdk-12\">non-SDK interfaces</a>, and as always your feedback and <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/app-compatibility/restrictions-non-sdk-interfaces#feature-request\">requests for public API equivalents</a> are welcome. </p> <p> <strong>Easier testing and debugging of changes</strong> - To make it easier for you to test the opt-in changes that can affect your app, we‚Äôve made many of them toggleable. WIth the toggles you can force-enable or disable the changes individually from Developer options or adb. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/reference/compat-framework-changes\">Check out the details here</a>. </p> \n   <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n    <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-OzooBPAi3i8/YC3BPS09IfI/AAAAAAAAQFs/Q2Afirbk_1cJut0YFYHqlsdpGmMv5YFhACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image5.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img id=\"imgHalf\" alt=\"mobile display of App Compatibility Changes with toggles\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1999\" data-original-width=\"1503\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-OzooBPAi3i8/YC3BPS09IfI/AAAAAAAAQFs/Q2Afirbk_1cJut0YFYHqlsdpGmMv5YFhACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image5.png\" /></a>\n   </div> <p id=\"imgCaption\"> <em>App compatibility toggles in Developer Options.</em> </p> <p> <strong>Platform stability milestone</strong> - Like last year, we‚Äôre letting you know our Platform Stability milestone well in advance, to give you more time to plan for app compatibility work. At this milestone we‚Äôll deliver not only final SDK/NDK APIs, but also final internal APIs and app-facing system behaviors. We‚Äôre expecting to reach Platform Stability by August 2021, and you‚Äôll have several weeks before the official release to do your final testing. The release timeline details are <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/overview\">here</a>. </p> <h1>Get started with Android 12</h1> <p> The Developer Preview has everything you need to try the Android 12 features, test your apps, and give us <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/feedback\">feedback</a>. You can get started today by <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/download\">flashing a device system image</a> to a <strong>Pixel 3 / 3 XL</strong>, <strong>Pixel 3a / 3a XL</strong>, <strong>Pixel 4 / 4 XL</strong>, <strong>Pixel 4a / 4a 5G</strong>, or <strong>Pixel 5</strong> device. If you don‚Äôt have a Pixel device, you can use the 64-bit system images with the Android Emulator in Android Studio. </p> <p> When you‚Äôre <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/setup-sdk\">set up</a>, here are some of the things you should do: </p> \n   <ul> \n    <li><strong>Try the new features and APIs</strong> - your feedback is critical during the early part of the developer preview. Report issues in our tracker or give us direct feedback by survey for selected features from the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/feedback\">feedback and requests</a> page. <li><strong>Test your current app for compatibility</strong> - the goal here is to learn whether your app is affected by default behavior changes in Android 12. Just install your current published app onto a device or emulator running Android 12 and test. <li><strong>Test your app with opt-in changes</strong> - Android 12 has opt-in behavior changes that only affect your app when it‚Äôs targeting the new platform. It‚Äôs extremely important to understand and assess these changes early. To make it easier to test, you can <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/reference/compat-framework-changes\">toggle the changes on and off individually</a>. </li> </li></li>\n   </ul> <p> We‚Äôll update the preview system images and SDK regularly throughout the Android 12 release cycle. This initial preview release is <strong>for developers only</strong> and not intended for daily or consumer use, so we're making it available by <strong>manual download only</strong>. You can flash a factory image to your Pixel device, or you can sideload an OTA image to a Pixel device running Android 11, in which case you won‚Äôt need to unlock your bootloader or wipe data. Either way, once you‚Äôve manually installed a preview build, you‚Äôll automatically get future updates over-the-air for all later previews and Betas. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/get\">More here</a>. </p> <p> As we get closer to a final product, we'll be inviting consumers to try it out as well, and we'll open up enrollments through Android Beta at that time. Stay tuned for details, but for now please note that <strong>Android Beta is not currently available for Android 12</strong>. </p> <p> For complete information, <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12\">visit the Android 12 developer site</a>. </p>\n   <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n    <a 12:52:23","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:52:23","title":"Sub-dollar pricing expansion in 20 markets","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/Ihp8sWyowEk/sub-dollar-pricing-expansion-in-20.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jkTn2ZC7zIU/YD_sw3mEKPI/AAAAAAAAQNs/XXGD0lIZOukqTELwRlVGkv19n2ZJkvHKgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/google-play-sub-dollar-pricing-v3.png\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jkTn2ZC7zIU/YD_sw3mEKPI/AAAAAAAAQNs/XXGD0lIZOukqTELwRlVGkv19n2ZJkvHKgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/google-play-sub-dollar-pricing-v3.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Neethi Thomas, Dafna Gal and Ashnil Dixit, Google Play </em><p> <p> At Google Play, we‚Äôre committed to giving Android developers access to the largest possible market for your apps and games. Google Play already supports free and paid apps in over 165 markets. We had previously lowered minimum prices developers can set for their products for 20 markets like India and Brazil. Today, we‚Äôre happy to announce that we have reduced the <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googleplay/android-developer/table/3541286\">minimum price limit for products in 20 more markets</a> across Latin America, EMEA, and APAC. </p> <p> With these new lower limits, you can now set prices in the range of 10-30 cents US equivalent in most of these markets. These ultra-low price points, or ‚Äúsub-dollar‚Äù prices, allow you to reach new potential buyers by adjusting your pricing to better reflect local purchasing power and demand. It also gives you more flexibility to set your global pricing strategy and gives more users the opportunity to enjoy monetized experiences in your apps and games.<br><br>The minimum price limit for paid apps, in-app products, and subscriptions has been lowered in these new markets: Bangladesh, Bulgaria, Bolivia, Costa Rica, Czech Republic, Denmark, Croatia, Hungary, Jordan, Kazakhstan, Lebanon, Sri Lanka, Myanmar, Pakistan, Paraguay, Romania, Serbia, Thailand, Tanzania and Vietnam. </br></br></p> <p> Additional markets where sub-dollar pricing is available: Brazil, Chile, Colombia, Egypt, India, Indonesia, Malaysia, Mexico, Nigeria, Peru, Philippines, Poland, Russia, Saudi Arabia, South Africa, Turkey and Ukraine<br><br>To adjust your prices in Google Play Console, please see our <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googleplay/android-developer/answer/6334373\">Help Center article</a>. The full list of price ranges can be found <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googleplay/android-developer/table/3541286?rd=1\">here</a>. </br></br></p> <p> <strong><br>Best practices for sub-dollar pricing</br></strong> </p> <p> Since the feature was introduced in 2015, Android developers have been using sub-dollar pricing to expand their paying user base in creative ways. Here are a few ways you can use sub-dollar pricing to help grow your own business: </p> \n    <ul> \n     <li><strong>Try offering limited-time promotions. </strong>Sub-dollar pricing is a great tool to entice new users through promotions, or to reward loyal users with low-cost perks. For example, to convert more paying users of their popular game <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.igg.android.lordsmobile\">Lords Mobile</a>, developer IGG sometimes offers special bundles for only IDR 3000 (USD 0.20) that offer 2-3x more value for a limited time. Because these are special offers, it allowed them to expand their payer base without cannibalization.<br> <li><strong>Offer seasonal deals. </strong>Sub-dollar pricing is also useful for seasonal sales. Because users know they have a limited opportunity to buy these items, it makes them more attractive. Combined with the low price, it can be an attractive offer for first time buyers. Moonton offers rare skins when users make their first purchase of the season in Mobile Legends, even if it‚Äôs a sub-dollar purchase.<br> <li><strong>Try introductory pricing offers. </strong>Sub-dollar pricing can also be used to attract new paying users with introductory pricing. For example, you could offer users who have never made a purchase a valuable item at a sub-dollar price. Developer Moonton does this, offering users access to popular heroes in their game <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.mobile.legends\">Mobile Legends: Bang Bang</a> when they make their first purchase. This strategy helps them reach new paying users without much impact on their overall game economy. <br> <li><strong>Reward loyalty. </strong>You can also try sub-dollar pricing in conjunction with repeat purchase events. For example, you could offer special bonuses to players making one purchase a day for seven days, without users spending more than they are comfortable with. <br> <li><strong>Offer gacha. </strong>Sub-dollar pricing works well for chance-based items, or ‚Äúgacha,‚Äù which can appeal to new users. Users who aren‚Äôt willing to spend $5 on a valuable in-game item may be willing to pay $0.15 to open a treasure chest with a chance of finding the item inside. By offering gacha at sub-dollar pricing, many users may be willing to pay a token amount just to try their luck. </li> </br></li></br></li></br></li></br></li>\n    </ul> <p> <br>There are many ways to use sub-dollar and localized pricing and the suggestions listed above are just a starting point. We‚Äôre excited to see how you‚Äôll use our features to grow your business. </br></p>\n    <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n     <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?a=Ihp8sWyowEk:k1Y6eX51ozQ:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\" /></a> \n     <a We covered ways in which you can use the API and the design tool to create rich, custom, and complex animations for your users. </p> <p> </p> <p> Check out the episodes below to increase your knowledge and skills in different areas of the Motion Layout API and design tool. And watch the live Q&amp;A episode, featuring engineers on the Motion Layout and Developer Relations teams. </p> <h2>Episode 1 - ConstraintSet Animations</h2> <p> This video explores how ConstraintSets are used to define different states of your UI that you animate between. Along the way, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/objcode?lang=en\">Sean</a> shows how to use Motion Editor in Android Studio to create and edit these transitions. </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/M1jE3W3_NTQ\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <h2>Episode 2 - Keyframes</h2> <p> This episode shows how to use Keyframes in a MotionLayout animation to customize the animation by altering the values of various properties over time. For example, you can use keyframes to change the path an object takes between start and end, instead of following just the default linear path it would follow otherwise. </p> \n    <center>\n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/n_om_WcfSOM\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe>\n    </center> <h2>Episode 3 - Multiple ConstraintSets</h2> <p> In this third episode, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/objcode?lang=en\">Sean</a> shows how you can add ConstraintSets, beyond the default two (start + end) to create more complex animations, or transitions that flow through multiple states between the start and end. </p> <p> \n     <center> \n      <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/k2HyX6fd_as\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n     </center> <h2>Episode 4 - Building a Collapsible Header</h2> <p> In the fourth episode, explains how to build a collapsible toolbar using Motion Layout, which is a common place where this API shines. Along the way, you'll learn how to animate custom attributes using MotionLayout. </p> \n     <center> \n      <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/xXR9bOHJ648\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n     </center> <h2>Episode 5 - Live Q&amp;A</h2> <p> The final episode of the series was a live Q&amp;A, streamed and recorded on February 18th. It‚Äôs too late to see it or ask your questions live, but check out the recording to watch the conversation between me (asking the Qs) and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/objcode?lang=en\">Sean</a>, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/johnhoford?ref_src=twsrc%5Egoogle%7Ctwcamp%5Eserp%7Ctwgr%5Eauthor\">John</a>, and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/camaelon?lang=en\">Nicolas</a> (supplying the As). \n      <center> \n       <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/SZnL6VtYK3U\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n      </center> <h2>More Motion Layout Resources</h2> <p> There are plenty of other resources to learn more about how to use Motion Layout, besides <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLWz5rJ2EKKc_PEOEHNBEyy6tPX1EgtUw2\">this MAD Skills series</a>, including: </p> \n      <ul> \n       <li><a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=o8c1RO3WgBA&amp;list=PLWz5rJ2EKKc-bcyUTIFAr97ZtRkwM7S4y\">MotionTags</a>: This series of screencasts on specific areas of the Motion Layout API just wrapped up. <li><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/constraint-layout/motionlayout\">Motion Layout Guide</a>: This guide on our developer site provides a great jumping-off point with an overview of the API, code snippets showing how to get started, and examples of how to do various kinds of animations with Motion Layout. <li><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/constraint-layout/motionlayout/examples\">Examples</a>: This doc has several visual examples, alongside the XML it took to create them. <li><a href=\"http://androidbackstage.blogspot.com/2020/09/adb-148-constraintmotionlayouteditor.html\">ADB podcast</a>: I had a conversation with John, Nicolas, and Sean (not coincidentally, the same people who joined me for the livestream Q&amp;A on MotionLayout) a few weeks ago. If you want to hear more about MotionLayout and ConstraintLayout, check it out on the <a href=\"http://androidbackstage.blogspot.com/2020/09/adb-148-constraintmotionlayouteditor.html\">podcast site</a> or in your favorite podcast app. </li> </li></li></li>\n      </ul> <h2>But Wait, There‚Äôs More!</h2> <p> The Motion Layout series may have ended, but there‚Äôs still plenty still to come in the MAD Skills series. 12:52:23","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:52:23","title":"Creating custom Tiles on Wear OS by Google with the Jetpack Tiles library","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/YGwVP_qYyN8/creating-custom-tiles-on-wear-os-by-google-with-jetpack-tiles.html","description":"<p><em>Posted by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/lojanda\">Jolanda Verhoef</a>, Developer Relations Engineer</em></p> \n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-DSDGYNsZaxM/YEuUtUcECzI/AAAAAAAAQPE/NRSM2Brqtog0vtlHiDgIf2D4YVo16VK_wCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-Announcing-Wear-OS-Tiles-Alpha-social-V2.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Wear OS header\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1027\" data-original-width=\"2048\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-DSDGYNsZaxM/YEuUtUcECzI/AAAAAAAAQPE/NRSM2Brqtog0vtlHiDgIf2D4YVo16VK_wCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android-Announcing-Wear-OS-Tiles-Alpha-social-V2.png\" /></a>\n</div> \n<p> We <a href=\"https://blog.google/products/wear-os/tiles-wear-os-google/\">introduced Tiles in 2019</a>, and since then, Tiles have become one of the most helpful and useful features on Wear OS by Google smartwatches. They are fast to access, convenient, and designed to provide users with swipeable access to the things they need to know and get done right from their wrist. This also gives users control over what information and actions they want to see. </p> \n<p> Today, we're excited to announce that the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/articles/wear-tiles\">Jetpack Tiles library</a> is in alpha. This library enables developers to create custom Tiles on Wear OS smartwatches. These custom Tiles will become available to users later this Spring when we roll out the corresponding Wear OS platform update. </p> \n<center>\n <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-oeswRpsmMEQ/YEuXPHK7SZI/AAAAAAAAQPU/8Cg9VvjRqAcXv1JPEpF_3ZKfUKKtw6FzQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/final_604b96c373a68300b7cfa2c2_502404.gif\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:50%\" alt=\"Wear OS interface\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"740\" data-original-width=\"740\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-oeswRpsmMEQ/YEuXPHK7SZI/AAAAAAAAQPU/8Cg9VvjRqAcXv1JPEpF_3ZKfUKKtw6FzQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/final_604b96c373a68300b7cfa2c2_502404.gif\" /></a>\n </div>\n</center> \n<p> Tiles can be designed for many use cases, like tracking the user‚Äôs daily activity progress, quick-starting a workout, starting a recently played song, or sending a message to a favorite contact. While apps can be immersive, Tiles are fast-loading and focus on the user's immediate needs. If the user would like more information, Tiles can be tapped to open a related app on the watch or phone for a deeper experience. </p> \n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Yl0tC36k5RA/YEuS_YO0bGI/AAAAAAAAQO8/t2jcA5U9SOAZB5_4c1xwfdE54ogji8NjACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Tiles_alpaha_layout2.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Tile designs from Figma\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"900\" data-original-width=\"1600\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Yl0tC36k5RA/YEuS_YO0bGI/AAAAAAAAQO8/t2jcA5U9SOAZB5_4c1xwfdE54ogji8NjACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Tiles_alpaha_layout2.png\" /></a>\n</div> \n<h2>Getting started</h2> \n<p> Tiles are built using Android Studio, as part of your Wear OS application. Start by adding the Wear OS Tiles dependencies: </p> \n<pre><code>dependencies {\n  implementation \"androidx.wear:wear-tiles:1.0.0-alpha01\"\n  debugImplementation \"androidx.wear:wear-tiles-renderer:1.0.0-alpha01\"\n}</code></pre> \n<p> The first dependency includes the library you need to create a Tile, while the second dependency lets you preview the Tile in an activity. </p> \n<p>Next, provide the information to render the Tile using the <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/androidx/wear/tiles/TileProviderService\">TileProviderService</a></code>:</p> \n<pre><code>class MyTileService : TileProviderService() {\n  override fun onTileRequest(requestParams: RequestReaders.TileRequest) =\n    Futures.immediateFuture(Tile.builder()\n      .setResourcesVersion(\"1\")\n      .setTimeline(Timeline.builder().addTimelineEntry(\n         // For more information about timelines, see the docs\n         TimelineEntry.builder().setLayout(\n           Layout.builder().setRoot(\n             Text.builder().setText(\"Hello world!\")\n           )\n         )\n      )\n    ).build())\n\n  override fun onResourcesRequest(requestParams: ResourcesRequest) =\n    Futures.immediateFuture(Resources.builder()\n      .setVersion(\"1\")\n      .build()\n    )\n}</code></pre> \n<p> There are two important parts to this code: </p> \n<ul> \n <li><code>onTileRequest()</code> creates your Tile layout. This is where most of your code goes. You can use multiple <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/androidx/wear/tiles/builders/TimelineBuilders.TimelineEntry\">TimelineEntry</a></code> instances to render different layouts for <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/articles/wear-tiles#timebound-timeline\">different points in time</a>.<br> <li><code>onResourcesRequest()</code> passes any resources needed to render your Tile. If you decide to add any graphics, include them here. </li> </br></li>\n</ul> \n<p> Create a simple activity to preview your Tile. Add this activity in <code>src/debug</code> instead of <code>src/main</code>, as this activity is only used for debugging/previewing purposes. </p> \n<pre><code>class MainActivity : ComponentActivity() {\n  override fun onCreate(savedInstanceState: Bundle?) {\n    super.onCreate(savedInstanceState)\n    setContentView(R.layout.activity_main)\n    val rootLayout = findViewById&lt;FrameLayout&gt;(R.id.tile_container)\n    TileManager(\n      context = this,\n      component = ComponentName(this, MyTileService::class.java),\n      parentView = rootLayout\n    ).create()\n  }\n}</code></pre> \n<p> Now you‚Äôre ready to publish your Tile. For more information on how to do that, and to learn more about Tiles, read our <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/articles/wear-tiles\">new guide</a> and take a look at our <a href=\"https://github.com/android/wear-os-samples/tree/main/WearTilesKotlin\">sample Tiles</a> to see them in action. </p> \n<p> The Jetpack Tiles library is in alpha, and we want <a href=\"https://issuetracker.google.com/issues/new?component=460965&amp;template=1422653\">your feedback</a> to help us improve the API. Happy coding! </p> \n<div class=\"feedflare\"> \n <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?a=YGwVP_qYyN8:P7JPJ7q5KRc:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img
