March edition of #AndroidDevJourney, we‚Äôre highlighting Android developers from all over the world with many different experiences. Early this year, we launched the #AndroidDevJourney series to highlight our community on our social media accounts. Each Saturday, from January through June, we‚Äôll feature a new developer on <a href=\"https://twitter.com/AndroidDev\">our Twitter account</a>. </em> </p> <p> <em>For a chance to be featured in our April spotlight series, tweet us your story using #AndroidDevJourney. </em> </p> \n    <center> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-zI37wdZKqe0/YFzmG9rN3nI/AAAAAAAAQSQ/aCtnv8Rl8RoHRWIie5Cd05k5h2CXsVqvgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Karim.jpeg\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"wajahat Karim\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"1200\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-zI37wdZKqe0/YFzmG9rN3nI/AAAAAAAAQSQ/aCtnv8Rl8RoHRWIie5Cd05k5h2CXsVqvgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Karim.jpeg\" /></a>\n     </div> \n    </center> <h2>Wajahat Karim</h2> <p> <strong>Tell me about your journey to becoming an Android Developer and how you got started.</strong> </p> <p> <em>Since the age of 14, I was very interested in animations and graphic design. I used to watch advertisement animations or cricket match animations of player profiles on TV and wonder how I could create these. Later that year, when my sister purchased our home's first PC, I started learning Microsoft Paint and later Adobe Flash. I worked on Flash for about 11 years throughout high school, University, and my first three jobs in game development.</em> </p> <p> <em>Game development was and has been my first love in computer science. But, Android became something special for me. It was NOT love-at-first sight because I hated Android when I first learned about it. I still don't know why. Coming from a poor family background, I got a fully-funded scholarship through Prime Minister ICT R&amp;D Scholarship Program and enrolled in National University of Engineering &amp; Technology (NUST), SEECS Islamabad campus.</em> </p> <p> <em>In my 3rd semester, Android was at 2.2 Froyo. A company organized a workshop at our campus which was attended by high-level tech folks like CTOs, software architects, and lead engineers. University management decided to send three students to attend that workshop and I was lucky enough to be one of them. In simple words, the whole 3-days workshop was over my head. I was a newbie in C++ programming and didn't know anything about Java. And here I was trying to learn high-level Android.</em> </p> <p> <em>After the workshop, I decided that Android was not for me. However, the university announced an open programming competition for any technology. But they gave extra points for Android submissions. This was my calling. In greed of those extra points, I took up the challenge. I borrowed the only Android book \"Hello Android\" from my teacher, Sir Shamyl bin Mansoor, and tried to learn as much as I could. Somehow, I managed to submit my first Android app which I showcased on a borrowed laptop with a very slow emulator of Android 2.2. To my surprise, I won it and got Rs. 100,000 prize money. First thing I bought was an Android phone and my journey started.</em> </p> <p> <em>I started writing about it in a WordPress blog, organized workshops in different universities, made my final year project a 3D game in Adobe Flash, and AIR deployed on a Samsung Galaxy 10 tablet which had a new Android 4 Holo theme and the great Fragments.</em> </p> <p> <em>After graduation, I got an opportunity from PacktPub (a book publishing company) to write a full book on Android. This was the best achievement I ever received. I managed to co-author two worldwide published 300+ page books (Learning Android Intents &amp; Mastering Android Game Development) on Android in the following two years.</em> </p> <p> <em>Having about seven years industry hands-on experience in Android development, I spend a lot of time on writing and sharing my knowledge with the community. I mostly write on my <a href=\"https://wajahatkarim.com/\">website</a> and on <a href=\"https://wajahatkarim.medium.com/\">Medium</a>. Besides writing, I have been active in open source and have created some Android libraries like EasyFlipView, Room Explorer, etc.</em> </p> <p> <em>In 2017, I started doing public speaking again. At first, it was a little tough to manage time while working a full-time job and freelance contracts, but it was worth it. I got more and more active in speaking and gave talks at events like Google IO Extended Karachi &amp; Hyderabad in 2018 and 2019, DevFest 2019 Karachi, Pakistan's first DSC Summit, Kotlin Everywhere 2019, and other local events.</em> </p> <p> <em>From these events, Sami Kizilbash noticed me and nominated me for becoming a Google Developers Expert. It was a tough time because of a serious medical situation with my father at that time, but a year later in February 2020 I became Pakistan's first Google Developers Expert in Android. I never thought that I would be a GDE in a field like Android. It is a big honor and achievement for me, along with a feeling of responsibility to help the community in a better way now. Android development has been my life fuel, career, brought bread for me and my family and happiness in developing and delivering more than 100 apps. With more than 2.5 billion Android devices today, this is an excellent career choice with high growth and potential for upcoming students and developers.</em> </p> <p> <em>My GDE journey has been a fantastic one. I have enjoyed every moment of it, all the love I got from Google and fellow GDEs - including Joe Birch who actually inspired me to become GDE, Hasan Abid, Saurabh Arora, and Juhani Lehtimaki, and Saad Hamid who also helped me through the process. In all the chaos of 2020, it was a very talkative year for me, as I did 25+ online talks on Jetpack Compose animations concepts.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What‚Äôs one shortcut, tip, or hack you can‚Äôt live without?</strong> </p> <p> <em>I simply love how Mnemonic Bookmarks make code navigation so much faster and easier. When you are working on a large codebase, it becomes harder to remember which method was where and what was happening in another Fragment. Simply, press Ctrl + F11 and choose any number or character, let's say 1. Now, when you press Ctrl + 1, Android Studio will bring you back on that exact line.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What's the one piece of advice you wish someone would have given you when you started on your journey?</strong> </p> <p> \n     <center> \n      <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n       <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-k91kz0Wb7bs/YFzmZ1pgdBI/AAAAAAAAQSc/3BG0bfrZRnEVv9WoEClskWkAv6sUtAEUQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/bookmark_mnemonic_popup.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:450px\" alt=\"public virtual\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"243\" data-original-width=\"399\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-k91kz0Wb7bs/YFzmZ1pgdBI/AAAAAAAAQSc/3BG0bfrZRnEVv9WoEClskWkAv6sUtAEUQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/bookmark_mnemonic_popup.png\" /></a>\n      </div> \n     </center> <em>The Computer Science and Information Technology industry is changing and updating minute by minute. No matter what stage of your career you are at, you have to keep learning and updating your skillset. Android is moving at lightspeed, with alpha beta releases rolling out on a regular basis. So, it has become harder to catch up and learn. So, get a Twitter account, and follow the folks of <a href=\"https://twitter.com/search?q=%23AndroidDev&amp;src=typed_query\">#AndroidDev</a> and you will be amazed how friendly the Twitter developer community is. You will learn new things every single day while scrolling the Twitter feed. And most importantly, don't forget to give back to the community. It could be through retweeting, or sharing your own code snippets, or writing articles, creating videos, or giving talks. In the end, you will see the more you give to the community, the more you gain back. So, it's all worth it.</em> </p> \n    <center> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-90WAMe7ruX0/YFzmm632BdI/AAAAAAAAQSg/GsTxxhy_1mUhXZB8yvdUUxQoZlb0ZQGXACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Singh%2B%25281%2529.jpeg\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Himanushu Snigh\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"1200\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-90WAMe7ruX0/YFzmm632BdI/AAAAAAAAQSg/GsTxxhy_1mUhXZB8yvdUUxQoZlb0ZQGXACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Singh%2B%25281%2529.jpeg\" /></a>\n     </div>\n    </center> <h2>Himanshu Singh</h2> <p> <strong>Tell me about your journey to becoming an Android Developer and how you got started.</strong> </p> <p> <em>My journey started from my college days. I got selected as an Applied CS facilitator for Android by Google in my second year of university. Because of this, I had to take sessions and help students complete a set of tasks as part of Bootcamp. In my college days I was not very good at Android, so when the opportunity came I took it upon myself to gain some knowledge of Android and then help people with their tasks. Learning to build apps that would be used by a lot of people helped me choose Android as a career. And that is how my journey to become an Android developer started.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What‚Äôs one shortcut, tip, or hack you can‚Äôt live without?</strong> </p> <p> <em>I like to use the Macro shortcut in Android Studio.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What's the one piece of advice you wish someone would have given you when you started on your journey?</strong> </p> <p> <em>As a beginner in any domain, not just Android, please keep asking questions on how to improve and learn from people in the community. Some of them might not answer your queries but a handful of them might. And in this way, you can learn and grow from their experience and when the time is right, you might be able to help someone in the coming future. This is the key to success!</em> </p> \n    <center> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ABazPqCPWB0/YFzm3lUY-jI/AAAAAAAAQSs/9OBjJPb3n0gSAOKASGKrhx8ZKZ9R9ifHgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Famisa%2B%25281%2529.jpeg\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Oluwasegun Famisa\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"1200\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ABazPqCPWB0/YFzm3lUY-jI/AAAAAAAAQSs/9OBjJPb3n0gSAOKASGKrhx8ZKZ9R9ifHgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Famisa%2B%25281%2529.jpeg\" /></a>\n     </div>\n    </center> <h2>Oluwasegun Famisa</h2> <p> <strong>Tell me about your journey to becoming an Android Developer and how you got started.</strong> </p> <p> <em>My journey in becoming an Android Developer started in 2010, my second year of university when I had the opportunity to participate in a program called ‚Äú<a href=\"https://www.media.mit.edu/ventures/EPROM/\">Entrepreneurial Programming and Research on Mobiles</a>‚Äù (EPROM). It was a collaboration between MIT and Nokia, and my university was one of the campuses that ran the program. I did not study computer science, so the program was my first exposure to software development. I learned how to build J2ME apps and got exposure to different mobile technologies at the time.</em> </p> <p> <em>Shortly after the program, I got a work-study opportunity at iQube Labs, where my mentor - James Fowe, who was building a mobile developer community in Nigeria - sent me a bunch of resources and tasks for me to learn how to build Android apps. The Android OS around 2010 was Android Froyo and that was the operating system on which I ran my ‚ÄúHello world‚Äù on Android. Within the next year, I found myself building actual apps on Android Gingerbread.</em> </p> <p> <em>I have since worked as an Android Developer in different companies ranging from small to mid-sized startups with millions of users, to publicly traded companies, all across many countries. I‚Äôve had the opportunity of working with very brilliant folks that have contributed to my growth and learning.</em> </p> <p> <em>My journey is not complete without talking about the developer community. I consider myself a product of the community and that‚Äôs why I try to give back every now and then when I have the opportunity. </em> </p> <p> <em>I started getting involved in the developer community at my university - through various student groups, including my local GDG group then co-organized by Moyinoluwa Adeyemi (an Android GDE). I attended meetups and participated in developer challenges and hackathons.</em> </p> <p> <em><br>Becoming a GDE for Android is a career milestone I never saw coming. It started in 2016 when John Kimani (Google DevRel manager for SSA) toured my office and we ran into each other at the door. I wasn‚Äôt prepared enough to become a GDE the first time my profile was reviewed, but with feedback, guidance, mentorship and hard work, I became an Android GDE in 2018.</br></em> </p> <p> <em>I‚Äôm grateful to have had the opportunity to travel to so many countries around the world and meet members of the global Android Developer community. I‚Äôve also given talks at conferences and meetups; including DevFests, Droidcon (Nairobi, Dubai, Berlin, Boston), and 360AnDev, to mention a few, about topics I enjoy - Kotlin, Design Systems, Jetpack Compose, and Developer Productivity Engineering.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What‚Äôs one shortcut, tip, or hack you can‚Äôt live without?</strong> </p> <p> <em>That‚Äôs such a tough one, but I‚Äôll say my favourite AndroidDev tip right now is: use the Android code search tool - <a href=\"https://cs.android.com\">https://cs.android.com</a> - and Android API documentation as often as possible. (See also: <a href=\"https://androidsrc.dev/\">https://androidsrc.dev/</a>)</em> </p> <p> <em>The two resources have helped me in answering the ‚Äúwhy is this not working‚Äù question and understanding what‚Äôs happening under the hood. A lot of times, I need to really understand what the Framework function I‚Äôm calling does, and the answer is almost always in the documentation or in the source code.</em> </p> <p> <strong>What's the one piece of advice you wish someone would have given you when you started on your journey?</strong> </p> <p> <em>I‚Äôll give two for the price of one:</em> </p> \n    <ol> \n     <li><em>Structure and consistency are important when learning. One can‚Äôt possibly know everything, but one can try with enough of these two ingredients. Structured learning is becoming more and more accessible these days than it was, so one should take advantage of it, consistently - through codelabs, or courses and the likes.</em> <li><em>Get used to reading official documentations and official source codes. This is a valuable and transferable skill regardless of the technology one works with, so I would advise not to shy away from it.</em> </li> </li>\n    </ol> \n    <center> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-GGB6HNkbgBc/YFznJJDJ8PI/AAAAAAAAQS0/5kSKsulM8ewT3sopIfISwZQ__IpD-531ACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Pawlikowska.jpeg\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Karolina Pawlikowska\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"1200\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-GGB6HNkbgBc/YFznJJDJ8PI/AAAAAAAAQS0/5kSKsulM8ewT3sopIfISwZQ__IpD-531ACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/ADJ_twitter_Pawlikowska.jpeg\" /></a>\n     </div> \n    </center> <h2>Karolina Pawlikowska</h2> <p> <strong>Tell me about your journey to becoming an Android Developer and how you got started.</strong> </p> <p> <em>From a young age, I‚Äôve always loved science fiction books and movies ‚Äì I always had a gut feeling that whatever career path I went down, it would have something to do with computers. Programming quickly became my favourite creative outlet ‚Äì it started with creating websites and apps when I was 11, mainly as a way to enhance my other passions such as drawing and making puzzles for my friends.</em> </p> <p> <em>I got my first Android phone when I was in high school and immediately knew it would open a whole new world of opportunities for me, so I picked up a few books and found a few online tutorials which got me started with code on my phone running Android 2.1 Eclair.</em> </p> <p> <em>My first app was a flashcards maker. I needed something like that to help me learn English and I couldn‚Äôt find anything online - so I made my own!</em> </p> <p> <em>Thanks to a few of my passion projects, including a flashcard maker app, I managed to quickly land a job as an Android Engineer while I was still completing my Computer Science degree at university. I then tried working across a few other areas in software engineering, but ultimately, Android was always my favourite and ended up becoming my specialty! </em> </p> <p> <strong>What‚Äôs one shortcut, tip, or hack you can‚Äôt live without?</strong> </p> <p> <em>It‚Äôs not quite a hack, but I honestly don‚Äôt know how I lived before ConstraintLayout became a thing! Oh ‚Äì and Android Weekly‚Äôs <a href=\"https://androidweekly.net/\">mailing list</a>, definitely one of the best ways to get all of the relevant news and tutorials in the Android world delivered directly to you every Monday!</em> </p> <p> <strong>What's the one piece of advice you wish someone would have given you when you started on your journey?</strong> </p> <p> <em>Looking back, I definitely recommend putting effort and being really intentional about seeking out other Android engineers around you. Once I started proactively attending meetups and working with other engineers, my skills and knowledge grew exponentially. Collaborating and bouncing around ideas has always been my favourite way to find creative and innovative solutions to problems I‚Äôm working on.</em> </p>\n    <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n     <a content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-y_15uDfl9aQ/YEKqX8YieuI/AAAAAAAAQOI/_HDatKD-AaMqOJliShI7ALhvr0lyHiJIgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-03-05%2Bat%2B5.01.09%2BPM.png\"> \n <img <p><em>Posted by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ericakhanson?lang=en\">Erica Hanson</a>, Global Program Manager, Google Developer Student Clubs </em><p> <p> <a href=\"https://dsc.community.dev/\">Google Developer Student Clubs</a>, a program of university based community groups for students interested in Google developer technologies, recently started hosting study groups called <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/02/new-curriculum-for-educators-to-teach-android-app-development.html?utm_source=feedburner&amp;utm_medium=feed&amp;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+blogspot%2FhsDu+%28Android+Developers+Blog%29\">Android Study Jams</a>. The goal? Learn Android app development through hands-on codelabs in an online curriculum provided by Google. There are two tracks: one for students who are new to programming, and one for those who already have experience. Interested in participating? <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/teach#for-facilitators-leading-a-community-group\">Facilitator materials are available</a> for anyone to host Android Study Jams in their community - take a look and get to building. </p> <p> Google Developer Student Clubs are dedicated to helping students learn programming together, among peers, in a fun and interactive setting. While over 50 thousand students from all over the world have participated in these Android workshops, we wanted to highlight the exciting work from groups in Indonesia, Turkey, and Nigeria. From programming in <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/kotlin\">Kotlin</a> to building a series of apps, these students have put their minds to work. </p> <p> Learn more about what these three clubs have been up to below. </p> <p> <strong>Indonesia</strong> </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-L7_l8QGGaf4/YDex8zHfyHI/AAAAAAAAQJo/q022kr26MU8lx9ZEUzy63J9KyRdvkO7FACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-02-23%2Bat%2B10.53.23%2BAM.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-L7_l8QGGaf4/YDex8zHfyHI/AAAAAAAAQJo/q022kr26MU8lx9ZEUzy63J9KyRdvkO7FACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-02-23%2Bat%2B10.53.23%2BAM.png\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <p id=\"imgCaption\">(Image from UNPNVJ‚Äôs Android Study Jams where students are learning Kotlin)</p> <p> Club members from Universitas Pembangunan Nasional Veteran Jakarta in Indonesia recently came together to host a <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=T0KIY3d2Jio\">virtual Android Study Jams session </a>with over 60 students to learn the basics of building Android apps. Their student-run learning session covered several topics, including: </p> \n    <ul> \n     <li>An introduction to developing for Android <li>An introduction to coding in the Kotlin programming language <li>A tutorial on setting up and working in Android Studio </li> </li></li>\n    </ul> <p> After the students felt comfortable with the basics of Kotlin and <a \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"960\" data-original-width=\"1920\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-JIgrmrC09KI/YCVmfeDzHzI/AAAAAAAAQEc/01TyuWwB-NoLzm5wIqDYEyyNKSXCxBeewCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/app%2Bquality.001.png\" /></a>\n     </div> \n    </center> <p> Since the launch of Android more than 10 years ago, the platform and the user‚Äôs expectations have grown. There are improvements from user experience through <a href=\"https://material.io/design\">material design</a> to the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/privacy\">importance and advancement in privacy</a>. We know you want your apps to offer a great user experience. At the same time, we also know that it‚Äôs not always straightforward to know which area to tackle first. That‚Äôs why we are launching a <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/quality\">new App Quality section</a> in our developer site to help you keep up-to-date with key aspects of app quality and provide related resources. </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/QxyvS1oZOUs\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <p> In the first release, we have updated <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/docs/quality-guidelines/core-app-quality\">the Core App Quality checklist</a> to take into account recent Android releases as well as the current trends of the app ecosystem. Here are some highlights in this update: </p> \n    <ul> \n     <li><strong>Visual Experience</strong> - We highlight the best practice of using <a href=\"https://material.io/components\">Material Design Components</a> in place of platform components such as buttons. This will give your app a modern look as well as making features such as <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/ui/look-and-feel/darktheme\">dark theme</a> easy to implement. In addition to advice on back stack, we have expanded it to preserving the state of the app. This is becoming more important as edge-to-edge screens and gesture navigation are becoming commonplace, even in entry level phones. <li><strong>Functionality</strong> - There are three areas where we have updated our guidance. For media applications, we have updated our recommendations around the playback experience as well as support for HEVC video compression for video encoding. For sharing between apps, we highlight the importance of using the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/sharing/send\">Android Sharesheet</a>. This will be critical going forward as apps will <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/basics/intents/package-visibility-use-cases\">have limited visibility to other installed apps</a> in API level 30 by default. Lastly, we expanded our recommendations around <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/oreo/background#services\">background services</a>. Helping users to conserve battery is a priority for Android, and we will continue to share updates on this topic. <li><strong>Performance &amp; Stability</strong> - We have added tooling now available such as <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/topic/performance/vitals\">Android vitals</a> in the Google Play Console. One important point to highlight here is Application Not Responding (ANR). ANRs are caused by threading issues and are something developers can fixed. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/topic/performance/vitals/anr\">The ANR troubleshooting guide</a> can help you diagnose and resolve any ANRs that exist in the app. <li><strong>Privacy &amp; Security</strong> - We have summarized our latest recommendations to take into account the latest safeguards from runtime permission to securely using WebView. We have also expanded to include privacy norms that users come to expect from protecting private data to not using any non-resettable hardware Ids. <li><strong>Google Play</strong> - In this section, we highlight some of the most important policies for developers and link you to more information on the guidelines. </li> </li></li></li></li>\n    </ul> <p> Going forward, we aim to update this list on a quarterly basis to make sure this is up-to-date. In addition, we will be updating the quality checklists for other form factors. </p> <p> We are working on additional tools and best practices to make it easier for you to build quality applications on Android. We can‚Äôt wait to introduce these new improvements to you. Stay tuned! </p> \n    <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n     <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?a=PSUcLn3UO6M:R-TFA5KesNg:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img \n  </center> <p> Today, we‚Äôre launching the beta release of <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose\">Jetpack Compose</a>, our new UI toolkit designed to make it faster and easier to build native apps across all Android platforms. Compose offers modern, declarative Kotlin APIs, helping you build beautiful, responsive apps with way less code. Built to integrate with existing Android apps and Jetpack libraries, you can adopt Compose at your own pace by combining Android Views and Compose. </p> <p> With this beta release, Compose is API complete and has all the features you need to build production-ready apps. Beta also means API stable, so we won‚Äôt change or remove APIs. Now is a great time to start learning Compose and begin planning for how you will use it in an upcoming project or feature once it reaches 1.0 later this year. </p> \n  <center> \n   <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/vRjJAWh6JPE\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe>\n  </center> <h2><strong>What's In Beta</strong></h2> <p> Our team has been developing Compose in the open with feedback and participation from the community. Since open sourcing development in 2019, we‚Äôve had 30 public releases, addressed over 700 external bugs, and accepted over 200 external contributions. We love seeing what you‚Äôve been building with Compose and have used your feedback and feature requests to refine our APIs and prioritize our work. Since the alpha release, we‚Äôve added and improved a number of new features: </p> \n  <ul> \n   <li>üÜï Coroutines support <li>üÜï Accessibility support for Talkback - support for other technologies will be in Stable <li>üÜï Easy to use <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/codelabs/jetpack-compose-animation\">Animations</a>, with a completely new API since alpha. <li><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/interop\">Interoperability</a> with Views <li><a href=\"http://material.io/blog/jetpack-compose-beta\">Material UI Components</a>, all with @Sampled code <li>Lazy Lists - Jetpack Compose's take on RecyclerView <li>DSL-based <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/layout#contraintlayout\">Constraint Layout</a> <li>Modifiers <li>Testing <li>Theming and Graphics, with easy support for Dark and Light mode <li>Input and gestures <li>Text and editable text <li>Window management </li> </li></li></li></li></li></li></li></li></li></li></li></li>\n  </ul> <p> For the beta release, we‚Äôve been focused on ensuring API completeness; that all foundational APIs are in place for us to continue to build upon for 1.0 and beyond. We‚Äôll work on stabilizing these APIs up to our 1.0 release with particular focus on app performance and accessibility. </p> <p> Compose Beta is supported by the latest Canary of <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/preview?gclid=CjwKCAiAyc2BBhAaEiwA44-wW02UxPzHservPxmOjAhKgYKMLmJF1vWR4Vvln4M6tZNIDgw2l3qDxxoCmawQAvD_BwE&amp;gclsrc=aw.ds\">Android Studio Arctic Fox</a>, which features many <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/tooling\">new tools</a>: </p> <p> \n   <ul>\n     üÜï Live Literals: real time update of literals in Preview and on device or emulator \n   </ul></p> <p> üÜï <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/animation#tooling\">Animation Preview</a>: inspect and playback animations </p> <p> üÜï <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/preview/features#compose-layout-inspector\"> Compose support in the Layout Inspector</a> </p> <p> üÜï Interactive preview: inspect and interact with a Composable in isolation </p> <p> üÜï Deploy Preview: to deploy a Composable on your device without needing a full app </p>  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4sRxCjW0pv4/YDVXZXFYDPI/AAAAAAAAQIg/oAG126nEJ2Qwv6pOCGZ_aMj3TgAvk3Y5gCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/live_literal%2B%25281%2529.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4sRxCjW0pv4/YDVXZXFYDPI/AAAAAAAAQIg/oAG126nEJ2Qwv6pOCGZ_aMj3TgAvk3Y5gCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/live_literal%2B%25281%2529.gif\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> <p id=\"imgCaption\">Live Literals on Android Emulator</p> <br> <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-DdXJJZEujIs/YDVX7L2lTzI/AAAAAAAAQIo/5a-W1_ZGStUsOVu-hSXKcRNrf9ds91LMACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/inspector_compose_v3%2B%25281%2529.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-DdXJJZEujIs/YDVX7L2lTzI/AAAAAAAAQIo/5a-W1_ZGStUsOVu-hSXKcRNrf9ds91LMACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/inspector_compose_v3%2B%25281%2529.gif\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> <p id=\"imgCaption\">Layout Inspector for Jetpack Compose </p> <h2><strong>Works with your existing app</strong></h2> <p> Jetpack Compose is designed to work seamlessly with Android Views, letting you adopt at your own pace. You can embed Compose UIs within Android Views and use Views within Compose. We lay out a number of adoption strategies in our <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/interop\">interoperability documentation</a>. </p> <p> In addition to View interop, we <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/libraries\">integrate with common libraries</a> to help you to add Compose to your existing applications‚Äîno need to rewrite or re-architect your app. We offer integrations with: </p> \n   <ul> \n    <li>Navigation <li>ViewModel <li>LiveData / Rx / Flow <li>Paging <li>Hilt </li> </li></li></li></li>\n   </ul> <p> The <a href=\"https://github.com/material-components/material-components-android-compose-theme-adapter\">MDC-Android Compose Theme Adapter</a> and <a href=\"https://github.com/chrisbanes/accompanist\">Accompanist</a> libraries provide integrations with <a href=\"https://github.com/material-components/material-components-android-compose-theme-adapter\">Material</a> and <a href=\"https://github.com/chrisbanes/accompanist/tree/main/appcompat-theme\">AppCompat</a> XML themes so you don‚Äôt need to duplicate theme definitions. Accompanist also offers wrappers for common <a href=\"https://github.com/chrisbanes/accompanist/#image-loading\">image loading libraries</a>. </p> <h2><strong>Thinking in Compose</strong></h2> <p> Jetpack Compose is a <em>declarative</em> UI toolkit, a paradigm shift from the current View system, where you describe <em>what</em> your UI should look like for a given application state, not <em>how</em> to produce it. Compose takes care of updating your UI when your app state changes, so you don‚Äôt have to manipulate your UI into the desired state which can be tedious and error prone. </p> <p> Built entirely in Kotlin, Compose takes advantage of its great <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/kotlin\">language features</a> to offer powerful, succinct, intuitive APIs. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/kotlin/coroutines\">Coroutines</a> for example enable us to write much simpler async APIs such as describing gestures, animation or scrolling. This makes it easier to write code that combines async events, like a gesture which hands off to an animation, all with cancellation and clean-up provided by structured concurrency. </p> \n   <center> \n    <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/Ef1xKWjA9E8\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe>\n   </center> <h2><strong>Learning Compose</strong></h2> <p> To help you and your team learn all about Jetpack Compose, we‚Äôve updated our <a href=\"http://goo.gle/compose-pathway\">learning pathway</a>; a curated list of videos, hands-on codelabs and key docs to get you started. Today we‚Äôre releasing new &amp; updated <a href=\"https://goo.gle/compose-docs\">documentation guides</a>, a number of screencasts and a new <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/codelabs/jetpack-compose-animation\">Animation Codelab</a> to help dive deeper into how to build with Compose. From guidance on <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/architecture\">architecture</a>, <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/accessibility\">accessibility</a> and <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/testing\">testing</a>, to deep dives into <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/animation\">animation</a>, <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/lists\">lists</a> or <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/mental-model\">thinking in Compose</a>, we have guides to help you get up to speed. </p> \n   <center> \n    <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/kdwofTaEHrs\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n   </center> <p> We also offer 8 <a href=\"https://github.com/android/compose-samples\">official sample applications</a> if you want to jump straight in and see Compose in action. We have simple to complex samples, each showcasing different APIs and use cases. Check the <a href=\"https://github.com/android/compose-samples#-samples\">readme</a> for more details. </p> \n   <center> \n    <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-3k0SUG6BWIA/YDWc78VVWTI/AAAAAAAAQI4/NXO2Dh0fJ5Qs2aZQ4p0R1fpIg_Nx_EMegCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/compose_samples.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-3k0SUG6BWIA/YDWc78VVWTI/AAAAAAAAQI4/NXO2Dh0fJ5Qs2aZQ4p0R1fpIg_Nx_EMegCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/compose_samples.gif\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n   </center> <br> <h2>#AndroidDevChallenge: learn Compose and win prizes</h2> <p> If you‚Äôre ready to get started with Compose‚Äìand also want to win some prizes along the way, <a href=\"http://goo.gle/AndroidDevChallenge-1\">check out the #AndroidDevChallenge</a>. For the next four weeks, we‚Äôll have weekly challenges designed to give your very own insights into Jetpack Compose, so you can fly through your projects. Compete to win new prizes for each challenge, with over one thousand prizes to win including a Google Pixel 5. <a href=\"http://goo.gle/AndroidDevChallenge-1\">You can read more about the first weekly challenge - starting today - right here.</a> </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/sZK3HSX4cRU\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <p> With Jetpack Compose reaching Beta‚Äîwith stable APIs and feature complete for 1.0‚Äîit's a great time to start learning Jetpack Compose and planning how you might use it in an upcoming project.
